“No, Rio, my god!” Jen shouted in horror as Alice cackled at her side.

But Agatha was smiling at her, tilting her head as she watched her and Rio had to do it. She had to just finish this glass, just put it down, just not spew it back up and Agatha would love her. Forever.

And she did. She placed it down harder than she meant to and she felt the gin repeat on her as she did.

But she held it together.

And she grinned lopsidedly at Agatha who was beaming back and laughing quietly, her whole body leaning towards Rio and both hands now on her thighs as she used her for balance and leant in to kiss her cheek.

The kiss was soft, more nose than lips as Agatha slipped slightly but Rio didn’t mind.

She’d take that kind of kiss from Agatha Harkness any day.

When Agatha leant back her hands were still on her legs and Rio felt hot below her gaze, but then again maybe it was the gin she’d just swallowed down.

“Rio Vidal, my hero.”

The words shot right down in between Rio’s thighs and she gaped a little stupidly up at Agatha, trying to focus in where her brain was trying not to make two of the most beautiful woman she’d ever seen.

But that was difficult with how drunk she felt.

Blue eyes flashed down to her parted lips and for a second Rio felt like throwing caution to the wind and closing the gap between them but Agatha had already pulled away and Rio was able to breathe again.

“More drinks!” Alice announced, waving her empty glass in the air where she sat, having clearly copied Rio in knocking back her own and Jen’s.

“Well considering I didn’t get mine, that would be nice,” Agatha said with a hint of a smirk and a wink in Rio’s direction.

Rio scowled playfully at her and poked her shoulder now she was sat oh so far away in her own chair.

“You told me to drink yours.”

“Well perhaps if you hadn’t made them so strong I wouldn’t have.”

Rio narrowed her eyes, still trying to figure out how Agatha’s brain worked.

She liked to tease her, she knew that much.

“Get it yourself.”

Agatha’s jaw dropped a little and suddenly Rio didn’t know if she were teasing or not as she smiled widely, her hand coming up to her chest in a dramatic movement.

“Moi? Little old me get my own drink?”

“You heard me.”

Agatha laughed and stood from her seat, offering a hand down to Rio unexpectedly. “You can at least come and help.”

Rio raised her brows but who was she to deny Agatha for a second time so she took her offered hand and followed her into the kitchen.

In the cool of the air conditioning she shivered slightly and went to rest against the counter as Agatha dropped her hand and moved about the place looking for superior alternatives to Rio’s lethal G&Ts.

“I can’t believe I drank both of those.”

“I can’t believe you did either.”

Rio laughed and rocked her head back, staring up at the ceiling as she fought off the threatening spin of the room.

“You’re a bad influence.”

“And you are going to have an almighty hangover tomorrow,” Agatha accused, a little closer than she’d been before.

Rio tilted her head back and raised her brows at her, seeing that she had in fact moved closer, her hand now next to hers on the counter.

“Your fault.”

Agatha smiled and bit the corner of her lip, “You’re a fun drunk.”

“Fun?”

“Cute.”

Rio felt her already warm cheeks heat up slightly and she wondered idly if Agatha were doing this on purpose; doing everything in her power to get her to blush, or suddenly feel like jelly in front of her.

“So?” Rio asked quietly, trying to pick back up some of the bravado she’d had whilst drinking two drinks in quick succession to impress a girl.

“So what?” Agatha asked in amusement, her fingers reaching out to just brush across Rio’s nails.

“Do you love me forever now?”

Agatha’s brows raised in surprise and she stepped in, raising her free hand to cup Rio’s cheek as she said in a gentle voice, “Yes, Rio Vidal. I love you forever.”

Rio knew she was placating her, toying with the sensitive emotions of a drunk woman, but it felt nice to be held this way by Agatha, to have her looking at her like that, to hear her say her name, to hear her say she loved her.

But Agatha’s thumb brushed her cheek just once and then she pulled away, and Rio reacted before she could think, she grabbed the hand on the counter and she swung her other round to pull Agatha to her, catching her in a tight but one-armed hug.

“Sorry,” she mumbled into still slightly damp brown hair, “can’t just say that and move away.”

Agatha released a breathy laugh against her and she squeezed Rio’s hand before she released it and wrapped both her arms around her. “Okay.”

Rio closed her eyes as Agatha squeezed her middle and she thought she imagined it for a second but Agatha had turned her head slightly and had nuzzled in by her ear.

Her stomach flipped for reasons other than the gin and she felt herself suck in a sharp breath, and the arms around her squeezed her before they loosened and Agatha pulled back slowly, holding Rio still where she leant away from her.

Blue eyes were still hooded from the alcohol and the long day spent in the sun and Rio moved her hand to hold Agatha’s cheek, watching her watch her with a slight furrow in her brow.

“I should,” Agatha breathed out, turning her head a little so her parted lips grazed the heel of Rio’s palm before she pulled away entirely and cleared her throat, “I should get you water.”

Rio could only nod, only feel the loss of Agatha from her arms and the ache of something she couldn’t name in her chest.

But she turned away and leant back against the sink, focusing on the soft noises of a glass being taken from the cupboard, the door closing, Agatha moving over, the water running, the glass being filled.

Agatha pressed the glass to Rio’s arm and Rio opened her eyes slowly to take it, quickly drinking down the water to try to keep the queasiness at bay.

Agatha had moved away, fetching other drinks for the group and by the time Rio had finished her water and taken a few deep breaths, she felt a little more confident that she wouldn’t be tasting that gin again.

“I’m glad you’re here.”

If the words took Agatha by surprise they took Rio by surprise too.

She hadn’t planned on saying them.

But clearly drunk mouths speak sober truths.

Agatha paused where’d she’d been filling a glass with ice.

“You are?”

“Mmhm.

“Because we definitely gatecrashed and you didn’t look much like you wanted us here.”

Rio tried to fight her smile but lost. “I’m better when there’s a camera pointed at me.”

“What changed your mind?”

Rio shrugged and tried to act nonchalant as she ran a hand through her hair, “Maybe the gin?”

Agatha smirked and turned back around to continue making the drinks, “Well I’m using vodka now so let’s hope your opinion doesn’t change again.”

“Never.”

Agatha glanced over her shoulder and Rio sent a clumsy wink her way which made Agatha laugh.

Nailed it, Rio thought, beginning to hum quietly where she waited patiently for the drinks to be made.

Soon enough Agatha was pressing one into her hand and smiling as she held her own up to cheers.

“To ruined vacations?”

“To thanking you first in my Oscar speech.”

Rio’s gaze dropped to Agatha’s smirk and she was so distracted that she forgot to take a sip of her drink. It took Agatha nudging her glass gently with her hand for Rio to come back to herself again and raise the glass to her lips.

“Aren’t you supposed to be some hotshot lothario?”

“Hmm?” Rio asked softly, swallowing down a small mouthful of limey vodka soda. Even in her drunken state she knew she needed to slow down a little.

“I’m not sure you have any game.”

Rio could only laugh at this insult and raised her brows at Agatha, swaying a little when she leant in slightly, “Why’s that?”

“Just a lil goofy.”

“Goofy?!” Rio demanded with a look of faux shock but whatever she was planning on saying next was lost in her own mind as Jen appeared back in the villa.

“Why do you two take so damn long?”

Rio hummed quietly, in spite of herself she smiled goofily over at Jennifer and Agatha laughed as she moved to pick up Jen’s drink from the side.

“Rio was just telling me how pleased she was that we are here.”

“Agatha was just insulting me,” Rio added with a playful glare at the back of Agatha’s head.

“Riiiiight,” Jen said slowly, accepting her drink from Agatha and watching the two other women closely. “Well the party’s outside so if you wouldn’t mind joining us?”

Rio only nodded and pushed herself off the counter to begin striding out to the terrace again, missing the look exchanged between Jen and Agatha. Jen looked confused and Agatha just smiled as she walked past, focusing on following Rio.

“You took aaaaages,” Alice sang as Rio arrived back at the table.

“Making drinks is hard work,” Rio shrugged as she sat down a little heavier than she meant to in her chair and took another small sip of her drink.

Jen and Agatha appeared only seconds later and Rio wondered when Agatha’s chair had moved so close to her own but she said nothing. She was only vaguely aware that where Agatha’s arm was on her own armrest and Rio’s hand was on hers, her fingers were now grazing Agatha’s warm forearm.

“I’m not sure I’m ready to get back to work again,” Rio said quietly as she cradled her cold drink to her chest, shivering slightly in the cool of the evening.

“Seems cruel to be so soon.”

“When do you leave for London?”

“Mm, Alice?”

“Day after tomorrow. Just enough time to,” she waved her hand vaguely, clearly the gin had hit her hard too, “y’know.”

Rio laughed a little and her fingers stretched until they curled around Agatha’s wrist, seeking the warmth.

Agatha didn’t move away.

“Call my mom and wash my clothes?”

“Yeah,” Alice said with a smile.

Rio hummed and closed her eyes as she relaxed more in her chair, her thumb now brushing idly over soft skin.

“Well,” Jen said, the most sober of all of them, “When we’re back I think we both need a detox cleanse. This is the most alcohol either of us have had in weeks. You’re bad influences.”

Rio only grinned, her eyes still closed and allowed Alice to take this one for the both of them: “It’s good to let loose a little.”

“Not as loose as Rio, though. Sex on a public beach?”

Rio’s eyes opened and she was suddenly aware of the place spinning around her, the only solid think she could grasp was Agatha’s arm beneath her hand.

“Hey, she was hot and I was horny. Nothing much to it.”

“That easy, huh?”

“When you look like this,” Rio turned to Agatha with a grin and crossed her eyes to make her laugh.

“Goofy,” Agatha confirmed and she moved her free hand over to run up Rio’s arm closest to her.

Rio only continued to grin at her, delighted with herself that Agatha was paying her any attention at all, let alone smiling back at her, let alone rubbing her forearm.

“Hey, hey,” Jen snapped her fingers across the table and both turned to look at her, “Tweedle dumb and tweedle drunk. You’re both goofy tonight. What’s happening?”

Rio laughed and leant forwards to place her drink down, groaning a little when the world lurched a little more around her.

“I should probably go to bed.”

“No, stay!” Alice demanded suddenly, leaning forwards to reach for Rio. “Stay, it’s our last night. Sleep it off tomorrow.”

Rio shook her head and briefly closed her eyes, “No, I need sleep.”

If she’d been cognisant at all, she’d have felt the soft squeeze of her arm before Agatha released her but she missed it as she stood slowly and waved in the direction of the table before making a wobbly path up to her bed.

It was best to go earlier, she thought. The night had already been full of temptation, full of a promise that could never become reality.

And she felt herself slipping closer and closer to being sloppy drunk.

To maybe just pulling Agatha to her. To maybe risking it all for a woman who’d already told her she had no interest in women.

So leaving whilst she had at least a brain cell still firing was the best option.

Rio woke in the night because a sudden chill in the room made her shiver beneath the thin sheet of the bed.

She rubbed at her eyes and hissed as her exposed hand felt the cool air hit it.

“Did I wake you?”

The voice felt far away, not behind her where it should be in the bed, but in front of her. And Rio opened her eyes to blink into the dim-light of the early hours and saw Agatha silhouetted against the pale moonlight of the little balcony.

“No,” Rio said softly, “It’s just a bit cold.”

She saw Agatha nod and watched as she dropped the lit cigarette in her hand, stomping it out with her foot before she stepped back into the room.

“You can stay out, don’t worry.”

“It’s fine,” Agatha said quietly, turning to shut the windowed doors and drag the light curtain across them. “Bad habit.”

“I didn’t know you smoked,” Rio said with a yawn, curling in on herself a little more to protect from the chill.

“I don’t. Not often anyway.”

Agatha moved back around to the other side of the bed and Rio turned to watch her as she opened a drawer and pulled out a little bottle of pills.

“What’re those?”

“I,” Agatha began and paused as she looked down at the little bottle in her hand, “I don’t sleep well. Doctor says it’s chronic insomnia and I’ve been this way since I was a kid so… sometimes I just pop a pill and it helps. I’d had too much wine earlier so didn’t take one.”

“Hence the smoking,” Rio concluded softly, frowning where she saw goosebumps along Agatha’s arm where she still sat in the cold of the room, her top half not yet under the blankets.

“Get under the covers. It’s cold.”

Agatha did as she was told and turned on her side to look at Rio, frowning a little in the dim as Rio reached for the hand that curled around the little pill bottle.

“Agatha you could have frozen to death out there. You’re freezing.”

“I’m fine,” she said softly, and Rio huffed, shuffling closer.

Perhaps it was the wine and gin in her system still, perhaps it was the vague haze of a disturbed sleep that emboldened her to do it, maybe it was just because it was the last time she’d ever get the chance to, but she pried the pills from Agatha’s hand and leant over her to place them on the side.

“Turn around.”

“What?”

“Turn.”

And Agatha did, turning back over onto her side, facing away from Rio in the same way she had the previous night when Rio had first shared this bed with her.

Only this time, Rio moved in behind her and draped an arm over her middle, aligning her body along Agatha’s to get as close as possible, in a selfless attempt to keep her warm and a selfish attempt to keep herself warm.

Their bodies fit together like two pieces of the same puzzle and Rio couldn’t help the flutter of need that settled low in her stomach.

It didn’t occur to her that this may not have been a welcome move until she’d done it.

And Agatha’s body had stiffened which made Rio regret her choice instantly.

But as if it had only been because it was a surprise, she soon felt her relaxing against her.

Rio smiled a little and turned her head slightly, keeping some semblance of distance between her face and the back of Agatha’s neck for fear she’d never want to leave this position if she didn’t.

But she turned into the pillow they now both shared and quietly breathed in the scent of Agatha that remained there, her arm flexing around her middle as she did.

“Rio?”

Drunk on the feel of Agatha against her and the soft smell of her hair, Rio hummed a response instead of speaking it and felt Agatha turn slowly, careful not to jog Rio too much as she did.

“Turn over.”

Rio blinked her eyes open and despite the chill of the air around them she felt her cheeks heat up in a blush and she nodded quickly, mortified that she’d been dismissed.

She turned onto her other side quickly and began to shuffle her way up the bed, feeling the mattress beneath her move from warm to cold as she went.

But just as she reached her pillow and made to move further along, a hand caught around her middle and Agatha wrapped her arm fully around her waist, tucking her fingers beneath Rio’s right side and pulling her back.

“Not that far,” she heard Agatha chastise gently behind her and suddenly felt the press of Agatha’s body against her, but properly this time, Agatha’s hold on her much bolder than Rio had dared to be.

She adjusted herself to curl her legs a little inwards and felt Agatha slip down slightly to curl her own to mould herself to Rio, the arm that was now trapped between them slipping below the pillow to support their heads.

Rio, who had been on the verge of slipping back into sleep not seconds ago, suddenly now felt wide awake, too conscious of Agatha Harkness wrapped around her for any hope of sleep to creep back in.

She focused on keeping her breathing even, but found it difficult when she could feel Agatha’s soft breaths against the skin at the back of her neck.

She cautiously moved her right hand up below the pillow to seek Agatha’s hand and found when she lightly brushed her fingers that Agatha reached down to hold her right back.

Rio’s heart leapt in her chest and she felt Agatha squeeze her waist, making a move to press a little closer.

She kept quiet for just a few more seconds before she spoke again: “You didn’t take your pill.”

“That’s okay,” Agatha murmured quietly. “I think I’ll be okay tonight.”

Rio nodded cautiously, not wanting to disturb Agatha anymore, aware she’d been the one to take her pills away in the first place.

But Agatha was warm and her body was soft against her and as she allowed herself to focus on that, she soon found that sleep wasn’t lost to her either.

There was no room between them for guilt over Agatha’s untaken pills, or for logic to creep in that this wasn’t a rational thing to allow for a person trying to fight a crush.

But when Rio woke the next morning, she woke alone.

For the first few seconds between waking and sleeping she wasn’t sure if she’d dreamed Agatha holding her all night.

It had felt so real, so warm.

But there was no evidence Agatha had even been in the bed, let alone curled around Rio as she slept.

As she turned to survey the room, she saw that even the little bottle of pills were gone.

Maybe she had dreamt it.

But worse than Agatha not being there, though that was definitely a close second, was the dull throb of a headache.

It felt like half-hangover, half-something else. And Rio didn’t need to guess what that may be.

Just as she was peeling the sheets from her body, the door opened and Alice bolted in.

“Oh thank god, you’re awake. We don’t have long. The car will be here in thirty minutes.”

Rio made a noncommittal noise and yawned as she followed Alice back out to the other room where her suitcase still lived.

She sourced a t-shirt and light sweatpants and underwear and then disappeared into the en suite to shower and change.

By the time she was done, Alice was now frantic in her haste to get Rio down the stairs and ready by the door.

“Yes, yes. Coming, coming.”

The dull throb of her head was back and wasn’t helped as Rio heaved her heavy suitcase down the stairs, greeted by Jen and Agatha who were lounging on the couch and armchair respectively.

Rio made brief eye contact with Agatha and found her smiling at her which eased her waking nerves a little but Alice was on her again and soon Rio was back in a dark mood.

“On the way to the airport we need to discuss timings for flights to London.”

“God, Alice. Can’t I just take it easy?”

“You’ve taken it easy for two days. We agreed that. Now it’s work time again.”

Rio groaned but her retort was lost when she felt a hand suddenly brush her arm as Agatha moved beside her.

“Technically, it’s still vacation time. I say at least until we’re halfway over the atlantic.”

“Amen,” Jen chorused from the couch and Rio smirked across at Alice, who didn’t look thrilled about being outnumbered.

“Fine,” she said with a huff, before pointing at Rio firmly, “halfway over the Atlantic.”

Rio only hummed her agreement and Agatha pulled her hand away as Rio said a quick, “thank you.”

“You’re welcome.”

They looked at each other for a fraction longer than was strictly necessary and Rio felt the same warm comfort she’d felt the night before. But this time Agatha wasn’t even touching her.

Just as Rio was about to turn away, for fear she’d stare forever, Agatha raised her hand to touch her cheek, “Did you sleep okay?”

She looked concerned, as if totally unaware that Rio had potentially had the best sleep of her life the night before.

The grin that took over her face at the absurdity of the question made Agatha frown and step back a little and Rio realised she must have thought she was making fun of her.

But laughter had spilled out anyway and Agatha was turning away so Rio had to scramble to get her to turn back, reaching one hand to her wrist and tugging to get her to turn back.

“I’m laughing because,” she glanced around quickly, seeing the back of Alice’s head close to Jen’s now on the couch.

They weren’t listening. They didn’t care.

But she lowered her voice anyway.

“I slept great.”

Agatha still looked cautious but she nodded slowly, a frown still present on her features.

“Good. I was worried you wouldn’t.”

There was the dull pain in her head again, and Rio knew what it was now: it wasn’t just about Agatha.

It was about leaving Agatha.

Because this little fantasy that she’d been able to carve out for herself whilst here, it was suddenly everything.

She cleared her throat softly and squeezed Agatha’s wrist where she still held it.

“And you? Did you sleep at all?”

“Actually,” Agatha started but was interrupted by the sound of a knock at the villa door.

Rio pulled away suddenly, turning quickly before she could change her mind.

This had to be it. This had to be enough.

She’d had one night of feeling like Agatha might feel even a piece of what she felt for her, and that would have to continue to be enough.

They all went out to the Mercedes van that had arrived for them and Agatha slipped in first, clearly used to having someone else always take her bags for her because she didn’t even bother to offer the driver any help.

Jen did the same.

Rio and Alice just looked at each other, then helped heave the last of the bags into the trunk and went around to jump in the car.

Of the six seats available, obviously only two were occupied.

The issue was that one person sat in the very back of the car and the other sat in the front row.

Jen was in front.

Agatha in back.

And Rio knew where she’d have to sit to avoid the wrath of Jen. And Alice.

She clambered in quickly, not wanting to draw attention to it, and took her seat along the same row as Agatha, sliding the seat in front of her back down until it clipped in at the bottom.

Rio slid her sunglasses from her head and relaxed back into the comfortable leather seats, pressing a variety of buttons until she felt the seat warmer switch on and she could rest her head back, bracing herself for an hour and a half in close proximity with Agatha for the last time.

The car was mostly silent the whole way there, and it turned out that Rio’s concerns were unfounded.

She and Agatha hadn’t spoken, they hadn’t even touched.

The next contact Rio made with Agatha had been when she’d lifted her suitcase out and their hands had briefly met over the handle.

It was fleeting, but their eyes met and Rio thought she saw a sadness in Agatha’s eyes that hadn’t been there before.

But Alice was pushing her along, making sure Rio didn’t dawdle through security so they could board the plane on time.

Alice, as usual, had timed everything perfectly so that by the time they arrived at the gate they were already ready to board.

Rio moved on autopilot, always aware of where Agatha was in relation to her.

Two feet away.

Right beside her.

Behind her.

The window seat on the other side of the plane.

Her only means of distraction on the long flight back were the movies in the entertainment system.

But halfway through the flight, three glasses of red wine in, she lost all sense of where she was and the danger she’d be putting herself in by doing what she did.

She put on one of Agatha’s movies.

It was her Oscar-winning role. The story of a ex-concert pianist cutdown in her prime by a car accident that left her unable to play.

Rio had seen it more times than she could count.

But it was comforting to see Agatha’s face without worrying what she was thinking about, or how badly Rio could misread the way she was looking at her.

“Really?” A voice came from somewhere above her. “This one? Not Susan Sarandon flying off a cliff?”

Rio sat bolt upright when she realised who it was, and narrowly avoided sloshing her wine down her front.

“Agatha,” she said lamely, quickly reaching to switch the little tv off, ripping her headphones from her head, though the damage had already been done.

Agatha only smiled a little, her hand resting on the partition that separated Rio from the aisle beside her.

“I just came to tell you that Alice is now sitting with Jen which I think means you’re safe from work chat at least until we land.”

“Right,” Rio said distractedly, her blush now taking over her face.

She took a shot and glanced briefly up at Agatha, barely able to make eye contact, but saw that Agatha was smirking at the sight of Rio looking so mortified.

“Don’t say anything. It’s a good film.”

“I know. I won the Oscar for it.”

Agatha bit down on lower lip and surveyed Rio for a second before she reached in and down, flicking the little handle to let herself into Rio’s semi-private booth.

Rio had turned the seat into a bed and so pulled her legs up towards her so Agatha had space to sit and she did. It felt strangely awkward between them, despite the fact that they’d been curled around each other the whole of the previous night.

And where Rio must still look mortified, Agatha looked cautious again.

“I think when we land we’ll be met with a whole bunch of press so…” she trailed off and Rio realised that she was saying goodbye.

She cleared her throat quietly and only nodded in response, reaching her hand out for Agatha to take. And she did, and held it in both her own.

“I’ll see you at the awards shows?”

“I’ll be the one in the fancy dress looking for a way out of there.”

Agatha smiled and dropped her gaze to their hands, her face softening totally until her smile disappeared and Rio watched, mesmerised by the view.

Agatha had taken her hand and turned it over slowly in her own, holding Rio’s hand palm up. She held her fingers above it, as if replicating that kid’s game of sprinkling imaginary sand into someone’s palm to see if you could get them to feel it.

But there was nothing imaginary about how she spread her fingers slowly up until they slipped between Rio’s and she entwined them again, her thumb moving to brush gently along Rio’s.

The caress over her palm sent shivers down Rio’s spine and she was so focused on the thumb now brushing her skin that she almost missed Agatha’s words:

“I think I’ll miss you, Rio Vidal.”

Agatha hadn’t looked back up yet and Rio was glad of it, for fear she might lose the nerve to say: “I know I’ll miss you.”

But she’d said it and Agatha looked up slowly, and when their eyes met Rio felt sick with it. Already at a loss for how to possibly get over not seeing Agatha every day.

But Agatha had a life to get back to. And a family.

And Rio had a life too.

They just didn’t belong in each other’s.

Agatha seemed to feel the same because she ducked her head and turned Rio’s hand over, pressing a swift kiss to the back of it before she stood just as swiftly, leaving Rio sitting all alone in her little cabin in the sky wondering how she could have been so stupid—because ‘happily married’ meant nothing when Agatha looked at her like that.

Chapter End Notes

My poor babies both having a rough time of it

The Favorite

Chapter Summary

Agatha gives an interview.

Rio gets an invitation.

Chapter Notes

Hope we all enjoy me using British spelling for the main text then removing any and all Us when a character writes

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It was 3am.

Two hours before her alarm would be going off.

And her phone was buzzing gently on the side.

Alice.

It had to be. No one else was able to break through Rio’s Do Not Disturb settings.

She threw her arm out of the nest she’d created for herself in the middle of her bed, slapped her fingers down until she could just about grip the end of her phone and pulled it back into the safety and warmth of her nest.

“Alice. What’s wrong?”

“Have you seen it?”

“What time is it?”

“Just after seven, why? Oh shit.”

“Seven your time? You bitch.”

“I forgot. This is important. You’ll want to see it.”

Rio groaned loudly, louder than she would normally, if her publicist weren’t on the other end of the line having woken her up. She wanted her to feel guilty.

“I have to be up in two hours,” she complained, doing the quick math in her head.

“You’ll want to see this. I’ve sent it to you.”

Rio huffed again and with her free hand she rubbed her eyes, shuffling her tired body until she was sitting up against the headboard.

“Watch it. Then call me back, okay?”

“I hate you.”

“Love you too.”

Alice hung up then and Rio briefly considered going back to sleep but knew Alice would be a terror if she didn’t do as she was told.

She squinted in the semi-darkness of her swanky suite and unlocked her phone. It was almost insulting that her iPhone recognised her face when it was this scrunched up and exhausted, but that was a concern for another day.

She had multiple messages in her WhatsApp inbox, some from random group chats, others from friends reaching out to see how shooting was going.

A couple from her mom she needed to get back to, and even one from her dad, which meant she really needed to get back to her mom.

She wasn’t the best at responding when not busy but when she was shooting and spending her time either on set or in bed, she became almost unreachable.

She clicked into the chat she had with Alice and saw three messages from only five minutes ago sitting waiting:
‘Wake up!!!’

‘Watch this. Call me back’

And beneath those was a link to a YouTube video from W Magazine entitled: ‘Agatha Harkness says “happiness” is movies with her son | W Magazine’.

The video was 4:53 minutes long but Alice had sent it so it opened to a specific time and whilst an ad popped up for some random airline Rio took the opportunity to pull the heavy duvet closer around her, turning her phone to landscape so she could get a better view.

She hadn’t thought about Agatha properly in weeks now.

Only when congratulating herself on not thinking about her had she entered her mind. Or when Alice was talking about Jen. Which basically meant she’d thought about her all the time.

So she couldn’t help but feel a little titillated at the prospect of seeing her face properly again for the first time in a while. Even if it were in black and white on her phone.

Even if it were 3am.

The ad finished and the video loaded and Rio was wide awake all of a sudden, watching as a black and white version of Agatha Harkness looked down the barrel of the camera at her.

She was wearing minimal makeup, her hair wild and… was it unbrushed? Rio couldn’t imagine a world where Agatha would allow herself to be filmed looking unkempt so she assumed it was the stylist’s choice.

She wanted to buy that stylist a three martini lunch.

Either way, she watched as her hand moved up to scrunch it slightly and Agatha’s eyes darted down as the interviewer’s voice started up: “Who is your favourite actor?”

Agatha’s lips twitched a little at the sides and Rio lost her breath as blue eyes moved back up to look at the camera: “Rio Vidal.”

“Can you expand on that?”

“She’s this ball of charisma, this wild and untameable force.”

Rio felt her cheeks heat up and her grip tighten on her phone.

“But she’s so calm when she’s on screen, as if she’s totally at peace with herself and what she’s doing. She’s naturalistic in a way that,” Agatha’s brow furrowed a little and she dropped her gaze in a look that told Rio she was thinking carefully about her next words. “…I so respect and admire.”

She looked back up and there was a smile threatening her features.

“Would you like to work with her?”

Her brow quirked and her tongue darted out briefly to wet her lower lip.

“Without a doubt.”

The interviewer had moved on to another subject but Rio had suddenly gone deaf, a violent ringing had filled her ears and she simply stared at Agatha on her little screen, watching her respond without knowing what she was saying.

She shut it down quickly and called Alice back.

“What the fuck.”

“My phone started to blow up and before I could even see what was going on Jen called to tell me.”

“What the fuck, Alice. She didn’t tell Jen? Wasn’t Jen in the room?”

“You know how W works those interviews. No questions before taping, no publicists in the room. Just you and the interviewer.”

Alice was right. Rio had done her own version of this interview not a month prior.

She’d mostly answered questions about her childhood, her hobbies, her approach to roles, but she hadn’t been asked about her favourite actor.

“Agatha didn’t tell her?”

“No. She had no idea.”

“I… I can’t believe she said all that.”

“I told you being friends with her would help. I told you it would work in your favour.”

“No,” Rio said slowly, frowning down at the soft floral pattern of her high-thread count sheets. “Agatha wouldn’t just say me because we were on vacation together. She’s not a liar.”

“Give me this one win, Rio. Because that answer will secure you a lot of support from the actor’s arm of The Academy, I know it.”

Rio’s heart was still hammering in her chest, the last thing on her mind the reaction of other actors to this endorsement by the one and only Agatha Harkness.

“Have you spoken to her?”

“No. But Jen was pretty pissed. Obviously she wants Agatha to win so-…”

“Can you get me her number?”

“Jen?”

“No,” Rio paused, second-guessing asking. “Agatha’s.”

“Sure. I’ll get Jen to send it.”

Rio went silent for a second and found herself twirling her hair as she stared absently towards the curtain-covered windows, “You think she really meant it?”

Despite what she’d just said about knowing Agatha not to be a liar, not to just say things because she thought she should, she was suddenly second-guessing herself. It was a big thing to claim: that Rio was her favourite actress.

There were so many greats past and present she could have named, that were far better. Industry legends and people with nominations and wins that Rio didn’t have. And yet…

“Rio, babe. You are so good at what you do. I was kidding about the friendship thing. And you’re right… Agatha wouldn’t have said it if she didn’t mean it.”

Rio swallowed thickly and closed her eyes, “I think I’m just tired.”

“Get another hour’s sleep and call me later. Remember I’ll be out in a couple days. You’ve press on Sunday so no partying. As much rest as possible.”

“Says the person who called me at 3am to wake me up to watch-…”

“And before I forget,” Alice interjected quickly, “your mom’s been on to me about getting you to get back to her.”

Rio laughed and shuffled back down the bed, “I’ll call today. Get her off your back.”

“Thank you.”

“Call me later, okay?”

“Night, Alice.”

“Night, Rio.”

Rio hung up and looked back up at her phone she now held above her head where she lay, far too wired to get back to sleep. A freeze-frame of Agatha stared back at her and she wondered what possessed her to mention her name.

The interview must have happened recently. Her own interview with W was filmed one morning and released the next week.

So she’d been away on vacation with her and then, what? Suddenly decided Rio was a good actress? That couldn’t be right.

A little modal popped over the top of the screen and Rio saw that Alice had shared a contact with her. Nothing if not efficient.

She clicked into it, using her sleep-deprived brain to give her enough courage and she saved the number quickly before tapping out a message.

‘A wild and untameable force?’

She didn’t leave her name on the message, and mentally kicked herself for not doing so but double-texting was more embarrassing than just leaving it how it was so she clicked out of the message and jumped back to the interview.

She rewound it and watched Agatha answer the question again.

Just as she was focusing in on the way Agatha looked into the camera, and looked away when she was thinking, a message appeared again at the top of the screen.

3:17am
Agatha Harkness: Who is this?

Rio sucked in a sharp breath and stared at the popup until it disappeared, debating whether or not it was a good idea to respond when she had to be ready for her pick up time in just over two hours and she’d barely had five hours’ sleep.

She lost the fight against her better angels.

3:18am
Rio Vidal: Your favorite actor.

If Agatha didn’t want to play ball, Rio knew she wouldn’t. She’d ignore the message or tell Rio she’d been taken by surprise and hers was the first name that popped into her head.

And that was fine. But Rio hoped she wouldn’t. She hoped she’d rise to the bait.

The thought of it sent a little jolt of thrill through her.

3:20am
Agatha Harkness: Aren’t you on London time? Why are you watching my interviews at 3am?

3:21am
Rio Vidal: Alice woke me to tell me the news.

3:22am
Agatha Harkness: That I mentioned your name in an interview?

3:23am
Rio Vidal: She’s thorough.

3:24am
Agatha Harkness: So are you texting to thank me?

3:26am
Rio Vidal: I don’t know. Would that make you respect and admire me more?

3:27am
Agatha Harkness: Don’t make me regret it.

3:28am
Rio Vidal: I think Alice is going to send you a thank you gift. Perhaps a selection of my movies for you to enjoy.

3:29am
Agatha Harkness: Go to sleep, Rio.

3:30am
Rio Vidal: If it helps, you’re mine.

3:34am
Agatha Harkness: Your what?

3:35am:
Rio Vidal: Favorite actor.

3:36am:
Agatha Harkness: Go to sleep.

Rio smiled a little at her phone, imagining Agatha’s expression as she stared at the three words of her last message. She sighed quietly and had to roll her eyes at herself for finding even the way she text to be attractive.

An ocean of distance, almost two months since Italy, and three timezones apart made absolutely no difference to her crush.

Knowing it wouldn’t help her case to keep bothering Agatha via text, she put her phone beside her on the pillow and curled back in on herself to try to force at least an hour’s worth of sleep.

She managed it, and slept soundly until the obnoxious sound of her alarm woke her to warn her she had thirty minutes before she’d be picked up.

In the scramble to shower and change, she’d forgotten about the interruption to her beauty sleep and only when she had a chance to check her messages in the back of the comfortable hired car did she remember.

Alice had thankfully left her alone between the hours of 3:30 and 5am. Only now was she messaging, knowing Rio would be fully awake and on her way to work.

5:32am
Alice WG: So many people want a comment about Agatha’s good taste!!!

5:33am
Alice WG: But think it’s much cooler if we ignore in any official capac. If any paps ask: say flattered, good friend, a huge fan, etc etc

5:33am
Alice WG: Get to set safe - call later x

Amongst all the other messages she was still to wade through, and Rio remembered with a stab of guilt she really did need to call her parents, there was another sitting in her inbox from Agatha.

4:59am
Agatha Harkness: When you’re back, perhaps you can thank me properly by coming good on your offer to play basketball with Nicky?

Rio stared at the message for a full five minutes, wondering how long Agatha had been thinking about sending it since her last message a full how and thirty minutes before.

But surely she’d not thought about it at all? Surely she’d just been thinking about her son or her son and basketball and randomly remembered that Rio, a few weeks ago, had offered to play basketball with him.

When they’d been in the pool together.

When Rio’s legs had been around her waist and when Rio had thought for a second, just a second, that Agatha may kiss her.

But it was too early to be second-guessing Agatha again.

She put her phone away and distracted herself by speaking to her driver, and used his chat to forget about the early morning surprise.

By the time she arrived on set, Rio was too busy to be able to think much more about Agatha’s suggestion. Though it fell into her mind every once in a while when things got quieter.

Being on set without Alice wasn’t her favourite place to be.

She had already made good friends with the cast and was friendly with almost all the crew too, but in her downtime where she could sit in her trailer for a while, she missed having her best friend around.

But setlife took over for a couple days and Agatha’s text sat unanswered in her inbox.

One evening she’d stayed out with two of her fellow cast members and had too much to drink for someone who had to be awake at 5am and know her lines the next day.

And in that precious time between falling into bed and falling asleep, she decided to talk to Alice about it.

She’d been struggling through like a pathetic loser pining after someone unattainable. She now knew she needed the help of her friend.

And so, halfway through the day on set the next day, when she arrived at her trailer for an hour’s turnaround where she could take a quick nap or call her parents (which she was still yet to do), she was delighted to find Alice already there and waiting for her.

“This place is a mess, Rio.”

“Shut up,” Rio said with a grin as she tackled Alice in a hug so hard she knocked them both down onto the couch.

Alice’s cackle filled the trailer and Rio felt at home in there for the first time since she’d arrived.

Still, Alice was shoving her off so she rolled away with a grin.

“Miss me much?”

“Like you wouldn’t believe.”

Alice laughed and her smile faded to something softer as she pulled her legs up beneath her and turned properly to her friend.

“You look tired.”

“I’m exhausted.”

“Wouldn’t happen to be because you were out until the early hours last night, would it?”

“Who told you?”

“I have my spies.”

Rio rolled her eyes but had her suspicions that it was probably one of the younger actors who liked his gossip as much as he liked his coke.

“Fine. Maybe I was. I just needed to let off some steam.”

Alice nodded slowly and watched Rio for a second before asking, “Everything okay? Lily says everything’s great, your performance is outstanding and she’s really excited for the final cut.”

Rio nodded in acknowledgement, pleased her director wasn’t just blowing smoke up her ass every time she praised her performance on set. But she knew Alice was giving her an opening and so she took it.

“Actually, I want to run something by you. Something that… well something stupid. But I can’t shake. And I’m telling you as your friend, not as your client, okay? Be my friend with it.”

Alice raised her brows but shifted and placed a hand on Rio’s knee where it rested against the back of the couch, “You got it. What’s going on?”

“It’s so stupid,” Rio qualified, already finding it hard to voice the embarrassing thing that had such a hold on her for months now.

“That’s okay. I’ve seen and heard you do many stupid things. And you me.”

Rio scoffed and ran a hand through her hair. “I have a crush. A big, fat, inconvenient crush.”

“Rio, not on Lily. You can’t screw the director.”

“No,” Rio said with a small frown, “Agatha.”

Rio didn’t know how she’d expected Alice to react but laughter wasn’t it.

“Right, okay, and who doesn’t? Half the population is in love with her.”

“No, look… it’s hard to explain. I just…” Rio cleared her throat and pulled her knees to her chest, dislodging Alice’s hand. “I think about her a lot.”

“Okay,” Alice said slowly, looking at Rio closely and with a slight suspicion in her gaze, “You know she’s married, right? And like, has a son and everything? With a man?”

Rio huffed and rolled her eyes, “Yes, people keep telling me.”

Alice frowned and began chewing on her lip, “Okay… Jen mentioned something a while back about you being a big flirt when Agatha was around but… it’s just a crush, it’ll disappear.”

“That’s the thing, Alice. I don’t know. It’s been weeks since I’ve seen her and-…”

“Rio, is it just because you can’t have her?”

“What?”

“Look, you’re a hot movie star. You can usually get whoever you want. And I mean anyone but Agatha… well she doesn’t want you and maybe that’s just it. You want her because you can’t have her.”

Rio blinked and for a second felt mortified, horrified that her friend had psychoanalysed her so mercilessly.

Maybe that was it. Maybe she was forbidden fruit and so every interaction she’d had with her Rio was reading into it, bolstering the fantasy.

Agatha didn’t want her. Rio wanted her because she didn’t want her.

She’d been wrong to read into the touches and smiles, Agatha simply found her amusing, knew she was flirting, and was secure enough to flirt a little back.

But then the was the way she kept close, the way she’d wrapped herself so securely around Rio that last night.

Because maybe Agatha was happily married but Rio was convinced she had even a slight curiosity about Rio. She knew she found her charming. She knew she touched her far more than she’d seen her touch Alice or even Jen.

But she couldn’t bring herself to vocalise all of this.

For one she’d be accusing a married straight woman of flirting with her which went against her general moral code and for another, perhaps she was wrong and Alice was right.

“Holy shit. That can’t be it, Alice. I’m… fuck, am I an asshole?”

Alice laughed, cracking the tension in the air immediately with the noise. “I mean… you’re not not an asshole.”

“God,” Rio put her head between her knees and groaned loudly, “all this time I thought I was going insane with it.”

Alice shuffled closer until her knees were just before Rio’s feet and she pushed at the top of her head to get her to look at her: “You need to get laid. When was the last time-… Oh. Is this why you went rogue and fucked some poor girl on the beach?”

Rio narrowed her eyes a little but didn’t have the strength to keep it up so flopped her head back down, “I was trying to get it out of my system.”

“Oh babe,” Alice laughed again, “Get over yourself. She doesn’t want you. I know it may be a shock to the system but just deal with it. Like the rest of us have to. Do you know how many times I’ve been left wanting?”

“Shut up, you do just fine. Besides, you have a hot girlfriend.”

“One I hardly ever see.”

“You’ve just flown back to LA for a week to be with her.”

“A week is barely any time at all. We were both still working.”

Rio just huffed a heavy breath and lifted her head slowly, reluctantly meeting Alice’s amused gaze, “You think that’s really it? I’m a dick?”

“Yes, I’m afraid so.”

“Did Jen really call out my flirting?”

“Yes. She said you may as well have crawled on top of her and stuck your tongue down her throat.”

Rio grimaced a little and had to fight the images that conjured in her mind.

“I wasn’t that bad.”

“I think she was just pissed that Agatha gave you that photo.”

Sighing softly, Rio fished her phone from her back pocket and clicked about until she turned it around to show Alice the texts from Agatha.

Alice read through them and raised her brows, “Please don’t tell me you’ve left Agatha Harkness on read for three days.”

“Maybe.”

“Rio. Get a grip. Text her back. Say you’re sorry you’ve been busy but would love to teach her son basketball or whatever.”

Rio rolled her eyes but stole her phone back and put it to the side, “I was overthinking it.”

“Clearly. Look, you’re both at the top of your game, you’re both used to getting what you want, you’re both hot. But think about it this way, if she were into you, it would never work out anyway. You’d have one hot night together and then it would be hell every time you saw her. At least this way you get to enjoy her pretty smiles and not worry about her icing you out of the industry.”

Rio hated to admit when Alice was right, but she was. At least about this part. And so Rio nodded and picked her phone back up to send the response that was three days overdue.

1:09pm
Rio Vidal: Sorry, work has been manic. I’d love to. After Venice I have a week or so early September back in LA. Let me know time and date and I’ll be there.

She turned her phone back around to show Alice and her friend beamed at her before snatching her phone away to check her call log.

“You ass. Call your mother.”

Rio laughed and snatched her phone back, “Dick.”

Alice, despite her teasing of Rio the rest of the day about her disastrous crush - whenever she got a chance between filming - insisted Rio have an early night so she could rest up for the following day of no filming but press instead.

The production company had worked around Rio’s schedule so that she could do press for All The Wrong Gods as the awards machine continued to pick up momentum.

What that meant, though, was that a usual press day of anywhere between 6-8 hours was now a full 12.

Rio was back to back with journalists from practically the moment she woke up, doing call-ins to radio shows, sitting in hair and makeup whilst she spoke to journalists in the room with her, heading for lunch for publications doing longreads, and sitting in a small stuffy room answering the same questions again and again about a movie she’d made over a year ago.

Her only respite during this time was Alice who kept her morale up by feeding her snacks, making sure she had plenty of coffee, and plenty of moments to complain when out of earshot of everyone else.

It was just after lunch with a journalist from The Times when the response to her message to Agatha came through.

Her phone had vibrated in her pocket as she hugged the journalist goodbye and Rio had checked it as she waited for her driver for the day to pick her up and take her back to the hotel where she was to do more interviews.

2:17pm
Agatha Harkness: 4pm, after Nicky finishes school, 2nd, 2270 La Granada Dr.

This time, Rio didn’t make her wait.

2:22pm
Rio Vidal: Looking forward to it. :)

She regretted the smiley face.

She didn’t receive a text back.

But that was fine. She’d sucked up her pride and decided that she would have to get over herself in order to get over Agatha. And she had over a month to do just that.

But a month goes by surprisingly quickly when all you do is work and sleep.

Alice was Rio’s lifeline, as usual, during this time.

She made sure Rio kept cheery during her ‘off’ days when she had to squeeze in more interviews that she’d ever done in her life. She made sure Rio had the right amount of sleep and the right amount of alcohol in her system at least once every two weeks to blow off steam but not ruin the next day.

She even convinced Rio that sleeping with the DP was not a good idea, which turned out to be great advice because the DP in question had a boyfriend and the boyfriend just so happened to be the Assistant Editor.

And Rio coached Alice through her pining for Jen. She helped her analyse everything phone conversation they’d had, every text that looked apathetic or every selfie where there appeared to be a pretty woman in the background.

It felt a lot like college all over again, where they were each other’s bastions of strength and support.

But perhaps the best thing Alice managed to do for Rio was to remind her weekly to call her mom.

And once this pattern was established, a grateful Anna Vidal sent a care package to Alice’s hotel room full of Puerto Rican snacks and a postcard from Delaware thanking her for managing Rio so well.

Rio was not happy about this and as punishment stole as much of the package for herself as she could.

But after filming wrapped and both her and Alice got so drunk at the wrap party neither was sure how they ended up in Rio’s bed the next morning in one piece, they still had another film festival to go.

Venice was a means to an end. A chance to campaign a little more in the European market but mostly to get Rio on the best dressed lists and get her face out there as much as possible.

Schmoozing. Rio could do it better than anyone.

And the best thing about Venice was that Wanda would be there, which meant Rio would have an ally other than Alice and someone else to complain to when it all got too much.

Alice had done Rio a solid and arranged for her and Wanda to arrive on the boat together, which meant that Rio could spend at least the first day of the festival with someone she liked and was technically working so Alice couldn’t tell her not to just stand gossiping with Wanda.

Turned out that this paid dividends for both Rio and Alice because whilst the press went insane over capturing the two of them together, Wanda had just finished filming on a set with a tyrannical director with a penchant for furious rages.

Which meant that Alice got what she wanted and so did Rio.

The gossip was so juicy that it continued into the late night as the three of them had dinner together in a small restaurant in the heart of the city.

“I’m telling you, I don’t understand how he’s still working.”

“He’s a man,” Rio said dismissively, swirling her Chianti, “and he’s considered a genius which is practically a pass for any kind of bad behaviour.”

“Rio, you don’t understand he was savage. At one point I thought he was going to go for the production assistant.”

Rio grimaced and Alice frowned at Wanda, “Did you have anyone come in to intervene?”

“No, a few of us-…” she stopped abruptly then because the waiter had come over to fill their wine glasses. When he was gone she cleared her throat and continued, “so, yeah, we rallied round, made sure everyone felt protected as best we could and… that was it.”

Rio reached for Wanda’s hand and squeezed it gently, “You could have called. I was just in London, I could have easily hopped a flight-…”

“Sweetheart, you never answer your phone. Plus if your schedule is anything like mine you wouldn’t have had any time to swoop in and do what, exactly?”

Rio shrugged but smiled a little, “I don’t know? Be a drinking buddy?”

“That’d help. Dealing with a maniac on a hangover.”

Rio laughed and pulled her hand away, “Whatever gets you through.”

Wanda smirked and took a sip of her drink before she turned to Alice with a sudden change of topic.

“So, Alice, you are in a lot of trouble with a lot of different people, I hope you know.”

This was news to Rio and apparently news to Alice who looked more than a little shocked as she placed her wine down. “Why?”

“Oh,” Wanda grinned and Rio relaxed instantly, knowing it couldn’t be bad if Wanda were getting enjoyment out of it, “getting your client to be announced as the best actress alive right now’s favourite actress.”

Rio scoffed and ran a hand through her hair, “It’s so offensive that you don’t think I’m just that good.”

Wanda laughed and Alice smirked as she leant back in her chair, “Unfortunately I’m not powerful enough to make Agatha Harkness say anything she doesn’t want to so that was all Rio.”

“That good,” Rio repeated, shrugging with a grin and making Wanda roll her eyes at her.

“Unbelievable.”

“Thank you.”

“Don’t think you’re winning though. It’s hers to take.”

“Oh, I know. And now Sylvia’s gone and said something racist it would be a miracle if she were even nominated.”

“I heard.”

Alice hummed quietly and glanced around them, cautious of any eavesdroppers, “It’s an industry town right now. Keep your voices down.”

Rio raised a brow and looked around briefly too, “I’m pretty sure everyone here is Italian and no one much cares what we’re saying.”

“Haven’t we had one too many lucky escapes with the press lately?”

Rio shifted in her seat, her eyes darting briefly to Wanda and hoping she wouldn’t pick up on Alice’s insinuation. But she did.

“What did they not get you on?”

“Alice, don’t.”

“What? You did it, the least you could do is own up to it.”

Rio sighed heavily and leant forwards towards Wanda, “I had a… moment with Agatha’s husband and then a… moment with a girl on a beach.”

“A moment? Is that what they’re calling it these days?”

Rio laughed and leant back again, “anyway, nothing happened so it’s nothing to worry about.”

“I don’t know, babe. It’s a little perverted if you ask me: sex on a beach and sex with another woman’s husband. Maybe speak to your therapist about it.”

Alice grinned at Wanda, enjoying having an ally in Rio-ribbing and Rio just smirked as she sipped her wine. “In case you hadn’t noticed I don’t swing that way and Ralph is… well I wouldn’t even if I did. Both very cruel friends.”

“You love us.”

“Unfortunately for me.”

So Venice went by easily, and Rio barely thought about her inconvenient crush at all.

She spent almost every second with Alice and now Wanda in tow, and focused her efforts on being as effortlessly charming for the interviewers and cameras as possible.

Every morning, Alice woke her with news of the previous night’s press.

“Everyone’s insane for the photos and you and Wanda on the boat. X is blowing up with people wanting you-…”

“Call it ‘Twitter’, please. We don’t like that man.”

“Yeah, yeah. Anyway, best dressed, best dressed, best dressed. You’ve practically won the festival.”

It helped a lot in moments like these, when Rio was exhausted in her bed and Alice was shoving her phone in her face, that Rio loved her best friend so much. She couldn’t imagine a world where Alice were just someone she paid and not someone she could happily see every moment of the day and not get sick of.

But by the time she was back home in her little house in the Hollywood Hills, Rio was determined to speak to no one and be comatose for two days.

The exception to this rule was of course Alice, though she was mostly busy fielding journalist requests and making up for lost time with Jen, and her mother, whom she called to tell all about the festival and to let her know she was home safe.

But two days of being horizontal soon disappeared and Rio, on the third day she was back from home, found that suddenly she felt rested and relaxed enough to actually be looking forward to seeing Agatha without the usual fear that she’d say or do something stupid or embarrassing - though there was always still that risk.

She hopped in the car with her hopes high that today would be a good day and called Alice on her way over, following Google Maps as she went.

“Hey.”

“Nervous?”

“No, I think… I think you cured me.”

Liar.

“Good. So all you need to do is not injure the kid and not try to kiss her or anything, okay?”

“Asshole. How’s Jen? You didn’t tell her about…?”

“Of course not. She’s fine. She’s away on a call with a studio. I told her I loved her last night.”

“You did? And?!”

“Well, she said it back.”

Rio laughed and grinned as she took the next turning, “Alice, I’m so pleased for you.”

“Not mad still we won’t both die alone together?”

“Nah, there’s room for Jen in our little beachfront retirement home.”

“I’ll be sure to let her know.”

“I’ll call you later, okay? When I’m heading back.”

“Sure. I need to talk to you about Late Night anyway.”

“Fine. Speak later.”

“Bye, Rio. Behave.”

Rio smiled to herself as she watched the little phone modal disappear on her car display.

Alice was happy, maybe soon to be settled. Miracles did happen. It was enough to relax her further as she drove the rest of the way to Agatha’s home deep in the Hills.

The street was quiet, with large houses spread along it, all white buildings with terracotta roofs. It looked not unlike where Rio stayed though the houses along here were, admittedly, much larger than hers.

Rio pulled up slowly in front of Agatha’s home and as she turned the key in the ignition to shut off the engine she felt for the first time in weeks a sudden nervousness.

It crept over her body slowly, so that stepping out of the car felt like a momentous task. But it was 4:01pm so she had to make herself move for fear Agatha would consider her late.

She stepped out into the afternoon heat and reached in the back of her little hybrid to take the gifts she’d brought for Agatha and Nicky, wondering suddenly if she should have brought something more, something grander.

But it was too late.

She shouldered her bag of gifts and tucked the basketball she’d bought with her under her arm, took one last deep breath, and made for the gate. She pressed the buzzer and chewed the inside of her lip as she waited for it to grant her entry, wondering if Agatha had any staff who would greet her before she had to come face to face with her herself.

But she didn’t have to wait long.

Ten seconds later the sound of the gate unlocking let Rio know she could push it open and she entered into a small court yard before a stately 1930’s villa home.

The lawn either side of the little walkway was perfectly manicured with palms and bird of paradise plants along the edges. And above the entranceway, creating a grand porch, were two stone pillars, framing the arched front door that stood open with Agatha Harkness in the middle of it.

Rio’s heart skipped a beat at the sight of her but she forced herself to remain calm, repeating Alice’s words in her own mind: “Get over yourself.”

“I wasn’t sure you’d show.”

“Are you kidding? Basketball and an excuse to hang with my biggest fan? What would keep me away?”

Agatha rolled her eyes but smiled warmly as Rio got closer and she stepped aside to let her in.

The impact of stepping into Agatha’s home was immediate. Even in the foyer it felt warm, comfortable, and it had Agatha’s signature charm all over it.

“He’s just out back,” Agatha said, answering a question Rio hadn’t even asked or considered as she turned to look at Agatha with an incredulous grin.

“You gotta give a girl a second to take this in. Your house is huge.”

Agatha laughed and hesitated for only a second before she placed a quick kiss to Rio’s cheek and then motioned for Rio to follow her.

Rio chewed on her lip as she followed her through to the kitchen, taking her around the large round table in the middle of the square entranceway with a fresh floral arrangement in the middle of it, trying not to focus on the faint blush she knew to be across her cheeks now.

Rio turned this way and that, spotting an inviting looking living area to the side with a mosaic fireplace and a door off of that, noticing the mirrors and art on the walls and the soft furnishings that gave the white house colour and comfort.

“Seriously. My place is tiny compared to this.”

“If you don’t stop talking about how big my house is, I’ll ask you to leave.”

They’d arrived in the kitchen now and Rio had a sinking feeling that her gifts would leave quite a lot to be desired at the sight of it.

“Holy shit,” she mumbled quietly, but Agatha had caught it and raised a brow at her.

“What? You’ve been to industry parties before. You must have seen some of the mansions in the Hills.”

“Yeah, but they’re all glass and metal this is… Agatha, this is gorgeous.”

Agatha seemed to soften then and she leant back against the countertop, watching Rio as she did a once over of the open plan kitchen, her eyes lingering on the breakfast nook just off of it and her breath taken away by the way Agatha had managed to make the space seem cosy, despite being in one of the largest houses on the street, in one of the most expensive neighbourhoods in Los Angeles.

“Thank you,” Agatha said with a smile that Rio returned when she looked back to her.

In her admiration of the house, she’d missed taking in Agatha’s appearance, which meant she’d almost forgotten her nerves.

Agatha now looked at her in a soft grey sweater, wearing light jeans and bare feet, fresh faced with little makeup and her hair up in an effortlessly messy bun, she looked exactly as Rio remembered: beautiful and intoxicating.

“I,” she started before she could be accused of staring, “I bought some… umm, well,” she shuffled and placed the clean basketball on the marble island beside her, and then fished in her bag.

“You didn’t need to bring anything,” Agatha clarified, folding her arms loosely across her chest as Rio pulled out her gift.

“My mom made these last time she was here. Actually, it was whilst we were in Italy. She comes and goes when I’m away just to get away, y’know? Anyway, she makes the best empanadas in the world so…”

She held up the large tupperware box and for a second felt like the biggest loser on the planet, offering the biggest movie star on the planet a box of her mother’s defrosted empanadas as a gift.

But Agatha looked touched and stepped forwards to take the box with a gentle smile, “You didn’t need to bring these.”

“You’re hosting. It’s polite.”

“It’s too much. I hope you kept some for yourself?”

“I’ve had a million.”

Agatha hummed and reached to touch Rio’s arm which sent a jolt of imagined electricity through her body that she wasn’t expecting and Rio flinched a little, playing it off by moving her arm quickly to run through her hair.

If Agatha noticed, she pretended not to, and went to put the box of empanadas in the large fridge opposite Rio, speaking as she did: “Nicky’s been excited about this since I told him you were coming.”

“Really?”

“Mm. Apparently I’m not very good and his father…” she trailed off as she closed the door and turned back around, “Well. He’s excited.”

Rio bit down on her lip and picked her basketball back up again, spinning it in the air before catching it once more. “I can teach you a few things if you like? So you don’t embarrass yourself in front of a seven year old?”

“Watch it,” Agatha warned with a smile as she made to swipe the ball from Rio’s hands as she threw it up to spin again but Rio was too quick and laughed as Agatha stumbled closer.

For a second it felt like nothing at all, the two of them, in Agatha’s kitchen, now less than a foot apart. And Rio forgot that she had a crush. She forgot that she couldn’t have Agatha. She forgot everything because she was close once more and looking at her in a way that Rio found she’d missed in their two months apart.

“Precocious,” Agatha accused with a glint in her eye and Rio hummed, narrowing her gaze a little.

“Not sure you can be precocious past the age of twelve?”

But Agatha only laughed a little and instead of trying for the ball again she stepped closer and placed her hands on Rio’s where they held the ball between them.

Rio sucked in a short sharp breath and Agatha’s brow furrowed just slightly as she watched her, “Come meet Nicky? I promise he’ll be worthy of you.”

Rio fought the grin for only a moment and then nodded, her fingers twitched beneath Agatha’s and her pinky moving to cross over Agatha’s on her right hand.

“I’m sure he will be.”

Blue eyes dropped briefly to where Rio held her little finger and Agatha seemed to hesitate before she pulled away, leading the way out to the backyard with a wave of her hand.

Rio picked up her tote bag again and followed her out, internally groaning at the hold this woman had on her.

It was insane to think that she was married to a man. A waste, she thought, as she stepped into the yard with her, and her eyes widened at the sight of it.

There was a wooden veranda directly off the kitchen with a little seating area with two cushioned chairs and a two-seater armchair. On the little table in the middle of them was a tray with five glasses and what looked like fresh lemonade in a jug and then a bottle of white wine chilling in an ice bucket.

But the view beyond this was what took Rio’s breath away. The yard was surrounded by tall palms and potted plants that dotted about the space, adding green to the area that housed a large rectangular pool with a smaller hot tub in the middle of it, raised up to create a water fall dropping into the crystal clear water.

Rio could see hanging lanterns in the trees and saw across the water another seating area with more comfortable chairs and sofas and an awning that gave it privacy and the cosiness she’d felt inside.

She glanced to the right and saw a built in bar and barbecue area and had to work hard not to let her jaw drop at the sheer opulence of it all.

“Stop staring,” Agatha said smoothly, turning to Rio with an amused smile, “Really. You’re being very uncool, Rio Vidal.”

“Agatha, this-…”

But she was cut off suddenly by the noise of heavy footsteps coming towards them and the sight of an out of breath little boy shocked Rio back down to reality.

Nicky.

He ran beaming towards them and threw himself to his mother’s side, but grinned at Rio as he pressed into Agatha and hid half against her.

“Honey,” Agatha said softly, placing a hand on Nicky’s back and gently coaxing him from his hiding place to stand in front of her where she could place her hands on his shoulders and introduce him properly to their guest.

“Nicky, this is Rio. Rio,” she looked up at Rio with a proud smile, “the best basketball player in all of California, Nicholas Harkness.”

Rio’s eyes moved from Nicky to Agatha and back again but before she could say anything Nicky had held out his hand to Rio, not saying anything but looking at her expectantly.

Rio laughed a little at the formality of it but stepped closer and shook his hand, grinning at the heavy up and down motion he provided.

He had long brown hair, tucked behind his ears and in a loose ponytail, dark hazel eyes and a slightly off-kilter shy smile.

Agatha had made a cute kid.

“A pleasure to meet you, Nicky. I hear you’re going to embarrass me quite a bit on the court.”

“Mom says you’re really good.”

“Oh?” Rio asked with an even wider grin, shooting an amused glance at Agatha before focusing back in on Nicky, “She’s exaggerating. But I have heard that she’s terrible so maybe I’m just better than her?”

“Watch it,” Agatha said again with a smile at Rio before she bent down to kiss a giggling Nicky on the cheek and murmured, “go pour us all some lemonade and you can play soon, okay?”

Nicky ran off dutifully and poured the drinks as Rio watched Agatha watch her son.

“Adorable,” Rio whispered so only Agatha would hear and she turned to her with a gentle smile, tilting her head just a little in acknowledgement before she touched Rio’s arm and stepped over to take a seat on the little couch.

Nicky settled on one of the chairs and Rio took a seat beside Agatha, placing the ball gently down so it wouldn’t roll away by the table.

“So,” Rio said officially, keeping her tote bag in her lap and turning her attention to Nicky as he drank from his glass of lemonade.

“Your mom didn’t tell me which team you supported. Which made bringing you a jersey very difficult.”

“A jersey?” Nicky asked in surprise, wiping his mouth quickly.

“Well, a true basketball player has to have a jersey when he plays.”

“Right,” Nicky said, suddenly serious and watching Rio like she were the Queen of the Basketballers.

Agatha, on the other end of the couch leant back against the arm, her eyes darting between Nicky’s serious face and Rio’s smiling profile.

“Now I only bought these just in case because I assume you have one already?”

“I have a couple.”

“Good! So what’s your team?”

Nicky looked concerned for a second, looking to Agatha for help and Agatha leant forward, her hand landing on the couch just beside Rio’s knee.

“Well, he’s between teams at the moment. I like the Lakers’ purple, his dad likes the Bulls.”

Rio grimaced and glanced around at Agatha who raised her brows at her, “Something wrong with either of those?”

But Rio had turned back quickly to Nicky and hummed pensively, pursing her lips. “Which do you like?”

“I… I don’t know. Both.”

“Okay,” Rio said slowly, “both is fine.”

She was about to follow up when Nicky quickly asked: “Which do you like?”

“Well,” Rio started with an amused grin, “my team has been the same team since I was about your age.”

“What is it?”

“Celtics,” Rio said as she reached into her tote to pull from it a green jersey. “I liked the green and my dad used to take me to games when he had the time.”

Nicky nodded seriously and Rio felt the brush of Agatha’s fingers just graze the side of her thigh.

“I like green too.”

“You do? Well, I have one other jersey I brought with me. And it’s a special one too because this is my best friend’s team.”

Rio pulled out the second jersey, holding it up properly for Nicky to take in. “Warriors. She grew up in San Francisco so this is her team.”

Rio looked down at the navy blue jersey hanging in front of her and then raised her gaze once more to Nicky who seemed to be taking this discussion incredibly seriously and she felt a wave of affection for the little boy.

“Okay,” he said slowly, glancing across at his mother.

Rio raised her brows and glanced back at Agatha before focusing back in to Nicky and asking: “Okay? Do you want to wear this one?”

“Can I wear yours?”

“Nicky,” Agatha gasped dramatically, removing her hand from the couch to place across her heart in a theatrical display, “And not your mother’s favourite team? That purple is lovely.”

Nicky grinned suddenly and Rio snorted as she leant back to look at Agatha, “Name one player on the Lakers.”

She heard Nicky laugh and from the corner of her eye saw him bounce a little in his seat but kept her gaze on Agatha who pretended to think for a second before she pronounced: “John Smith.”

Rio rolled her eyes but grinned at Agatha, batting lightly at her arm before she turned to Nicky and picked her green Celtics jersey back up, holding it out to him, “Fine, you can wear this. But just this once, okay? And then when you pick a team I’ll bring you the right colours, alright?”

“This is my team,” Nicky announced without a second’s hesitation, taking the jersey with a smile.

Rio opened her mouth to respond but didn’t know what to say and simply watched as Nicky slipped the too-large jersey over his t-shirt and grinned down at it.

“Yeah!” Nicky jumped up and motioned for Rio to follow him. Rio shot Agatha a quick wink as she scooped up the ball and went to follow her new biggest fan to the small patio’d area around the corner.

He listened carefully to everything Rio told him, he watched with a seriousness that belied his age, and he grinned with such abandon that Rio wondered if Agatha had ever grinned like that in her life.

It didn’t take long for her to become fond of him, and clearly Nicky was fond of Rio.

“One more point,” Rio pleaded teasingly, smiling breathlessly at Agatha where she’d been running around the court like a madman, trying to elicit the feeling for Nicky of being at a real game.

He missed, but only just, and Rio was quick to recover the ball and bounce it back to him, this time scooping him up and allowing him to score in an assisted alley-oop.

She caught them both, stumbling back a little in surprise but maintaining balance as she helped Rio to balance Nicky and soon stole him from her hold, making a soft noise of exertion as she pulled him down into her own arms and spun him around.

“A regular John Smith!”

Rio laughed and clutched her stomach as she caught her breath, beaming at the mother and son duo as Agatha halted her spin and let Nicky drop to his feet.

“Are you doing that on purpose?”

“What?” Agatha asked with an innocent smile, “He’s the best player.”

Rio was so exhausted that she couldn’t bring herself to argue and instead smiled widely at Agatha, only looking away when an excited seven year old threw himself at her and wrapped his arms around her.

Rio released a quiet ‘oomph’ at the sudden smack to her body but quickly dropped down to hug Nicky properly, laughing as he held on tight, his arms now around her neck.

“Come play again?” He asked quietly into Rio’s ear and Rio nodded gently, feeling strangely emotional about the request.

“Sure. Whenever you want.”

She pulled back only when Nicky did and saw in his face the return of his shyness that Agatha had told her about all those weeks ago back in the pool.

He didn’t quite meet her gaze again as he ran off to where the lemonade was and Rio was left standing with Agatha, feeling clammy and tired in the late-afternoon sun.

“You’re good with kids,” Agatha said softly, watching Rio with a kind of tenderness that made Rio want to turn away and hide from.

“I… probably just kids who like basketball. Or any other sports, maybe. Mostly basketball.”

She shrugged a little self-consciously and rubbed the back of her neck, mortified to feel that it actually was a little clammy and clearing her throat as she turned to where Nicky had run off to.

“He’s a good kid. You should be-…”

But her words died the instant she felt Agatha’s hands on hers and she turned suddenly to see Agatha close, holding her left hand in both of her own.

Rio felt something swell in her chest and couldn’t fight it as whatever the feeling was made her right hand move to rest over Agatha’s too, her eyes wide as she took in the face before her, wondering how she’d gone so long without being able to look at it.

“Stay,” Agatha instructed softly, not exactly a demand, not exactly a request. “Have dinner with us.”

Rio could only nod once, her mind a mysterious blank where it had just been firing on all cylinders, buoyed by the enjoyment of the exercise.

Agatha’s lips twitched ever so slightly and Rio felt her whole world stop as she leant in to her.

It must be what it felt like to die, she thought. Everything slow, everything wonderful.

As if she couldn’t take it in properly, her eyes fluttered closed and it was in the darkness that she felt Agatha’s lips against her skin for the first time in weeks.

Her cheek was flushed and she was sure it was a little sticky with the sweat from the past hour or so she’d been pulling out all the stops for Nicky in the Los Angeles sun.

But Agatha hadn’t recoiled. She’d pressed her lips to Rio’s cheek like she’d meant to do it, like she’d meant to anchor there for longer than would be considered a greeting in a European country or a friendly exchange between two movie stars.

But it couldn’t last forever.

And so Agatha pulled back and when she did, Rio’s eyes fluttered open and she turned her head ever so slightly towards her, seeking more of her warmth, wanting more.

As Rio moved and Agatha pulled back so slowly that Rio could have counted every freckle, their noses brushed and Rio sucked in sharp breath that caused the spell to be broken and for Agatha to pull away entirely.

Their eyes met and Rio saw that Agatha’s were darker than usual, her pupils swallowing the usual blue of her irises. Her lips were parted and her cheeks were flushed and Rio’s brain short-circuited when she saw where Agatha’s gaze was.

And then the world righted itself.

There was a shout.

A greeting.

A man’s voice.

Ralph was home.
