Fleetwood Facts

Chapter Summary

Ralph is home.

Rio comes to a realisation.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Ralph.

Rio had forgotten about the husband.

In all the work she’d put into convincing herself that she only wanted Agatha because she couldn’t have her, she’d forgotten about the main reason she couldn’t have her.

Her gaze fell from Agatha’s suddenly panicked eyes to the joined hands between them and she hesitated for a second before she pulled away, taking a step back and clearing her throat.

“Ralph?” She asked needlessly, watching as Agatha’s panic morphed to something different and she’d turned from her to march around to where Nicky had gone.

“He wasn’t supposed to be here.”

Rio felt suddenly like a spare part, no, like a mistress.

Without the obvious benefits.

She ran a hand through her hair and awkwardly patted her jersey down, though really there was nothing she could do to make herself look more presentable as she followed Agatha back around the house to where her husband had clearly arrived.

She was ashamed of herself but for what, she couldn’t really fathom. Maybe lustful thought, but those she’d had about various people since she was a teenage. Maybe that she’d half convinced herself that Agatha might return them.

Maybe because she thought if Ralph hadn’t arrived Agatha might have kissed her.

Waiting for them by the outdoor sitting area was a tall man with a dark sweep of hair that Rio recognised immediately as the surface-level polite husband of the woman she’d prefer to have all to herself.

A Clark Kent-type without the glasses and not for the first time Rio couldn’t help but see how someone, inclined to men, could fall for him. Which made it worse. But then maybe Rio wasn’t cruel enough to wish Agatha were married to an ugly man.

Maybe.

A red-blooded American finance bro with a strong jaw and a winning smile.

And Rio stood, a Puerto-Rican American woman with a basketball jersey that wasn’t hers and a light sheen of sweat across her brow.

Who would ever pick her?

Ralph turned to Agatha from where he’d been sat in the place Rio had been only an hour or so ago and gestured to their son, “Celtics? Really?”

Rio hated this guy.

“It’s my team,” Nicky said quietly and Rio shot him a reassuring wink as she stopped beside Agatha.

“I thought you’d be out all night,” Agatha said with such a lack of warmth that Rio turned to look at her, taken aback by this display.

“I came home to change,” Ralph said distractedly, now eyeing Rio as he stood and moved to offer her a hand, “Hi. Rio, right? You look different to the last time I saw you?”

Yeah, I’ve not been sat through hair and makeup for the last three hours you fucking asshole.

Rio shook the hand offered to her, refusing to look away from the man who so clearly wanted to say ‘you look much worse’.

“I just came over to test my skills against Nicky’s.”

She leant round slightly, and shot the boy a smile before looking back up to Ralph, almost daring him to say something.

The man seemed disinterested though, or else, already smug that whatever he thought the battle was, he’d won.

He had Agatha after all.

But Agatha interjected and moved just enough in front of Rio that Ralph had no choice but to turn to her instead, “You should hurry if you want to make your dinner reservations. Especially if you want a drink beforehand.”

“Actually,” Ralph said with a raise of his brows, looking past his wife and to Rio, “A lot of the guys in the office are fans of yours. I didn’t get to ask in Cannes and this might be a little strange but… mind if I get a selfie? They’d shit themselves if they-…”

Agatha had cleared her throat.

Rio opened her mouth and then closed it again, surprised by the request. But she couldn’t think of an excuse quickly enough to deny it so she simply nodded her assent and surreptitiously tucked her hair behind her ear.

“Excellent,” Ralph grinned and Rio once again saw what Agatha must find attractive in him. He had a boyish charm.

Superman in a suit.

“Honey,” Agatha said suddenly in a tone much softer than the one she’d used with Ralph earlier, “why don’t you go to your room? You can have an hour on your Switch before dinner, okay?”

Rio looked on as Nicky beamed and disappeared before the offer could be rescinded and Rio smiled a little at the sight, thinking that having been within Ralph’s presence for collectively less than twenty minutes she already couldn’t see any of him in his son.

And Ralph paid his son absolutely no mind as he reached over to pour himself a glass of wine, only pouring one for Rio and Agatha too when Agatha cleared her throat pointedly again and the man remembered his manners. “Excuse me, should be ladies first.”

“Where are you from?” Rio asked suddenly, accepting the glass offered to her without a thank you and trying her hardest to remain polite when all she wanted to do was run away.

“Dallas, originally. Moved to Chicago when I was a kid.”

“Hence the Bulls?”

Ralph smiled and thanked the universe that she was, fortunately, immune to his charms.

“Yes. Where exactly did my son get the idea in his head that Celtics was the way to go?”

“That would be me.”

Ralph took such a large gulp of his wine that made Rio raise her brows a little but he only nodded once he’d swallowed it down, “I suppose you can’t force a team on a kid. He’ll pick his own one day.”

“So,” he said suddenly, before Rio had even had a chance to take a sip of her wine, “selfie and then I’ll be on my way.”

Rio cleared her throat quietly and shot Agatha a quick glance and in seeing that she looked a little paler than usual she decided she didn’t mind doing this quick favour to get this man as far away as possible.

She shuffled to the edge of the couch and placed her glass down, and paused momentarily where Ralph had scuffed his chair along the stone slabs to push it back to the couch, holding his arm out behind him for Rio to slip into.

But Agatha had stood up before Rio made to move.

“Let me take it.”

Rio glanced around and saw that Agatha looked furious, her hand held out for Ralph’s phone, her fingers already twitching in a ‘give it to me’ motion.

“You’re the boss,” Ralph said in a tone that made Rio want to hit him.

But he stood and Rio stood too, allowing him to drape his arm around her waist and pull her closer than she’d have liked.

He smelled like expensive after shave and a hint of whiskey and Rio fought hard to force a smile when in interactions like these they usually came so easily.

But her gaze met Agatha’s above the phone she held to take the photo and when it did she felt the heavy weight of reality.

This was Agatha’s home.

This was Agatha’s husband.

Agatha took just one photo of the two of them and Rio decided she didn’t want to see what it looked like but she could bet she looked sweaty and uninterested in it.

“Here,” Agatha said as he held the phone back out to her husband, and Ralph took it with one hand, his other still on Rio’s waist.

Rio moved from his hold and went to stand a little further away, which Ralph didn’t object to, and Rio realised that he’d been holding her as if it were his right but that he had no real knowledge of his own actions: he was simply a man who was used to having a pretty woman on his arm.

But that didn’t sit well with her and apparently not Agatha either who’d moved around to take Rio’s hand and tug her in the direction of the lone armchair opposite where Nicky had been sitting.

Rio moved without question or thought and even sat down, looking up at Agatha as though to expect more instruction, but they never came.

“They’ll love this,” Ralph was saying with that same charming grin across his face.

“Really.” He turned to Rio and held his phone up like a trophy even with Agatha now standing between the two of them like an armed guard. “Thank you.”

Rio could only nod, smiling a little at the type of man who would consider the look on her face in the photo to be a ‘grin’ from a pretty girl and she brushed her hands down the tops of her thighs slowly as she watched Ralph turn back to his phone and broadcast the picture to anyone and everyone he thought would be impressed by it.

“Actually,” Ralph turned with that same, brilliant grin, “I might stay out with the boys. That okay, hon?”

“Of course,” Agatha said with a kind of shrug, and Rio watched as Ralph leant in and placed a firm kiss to Agatha’s cheek, making a ‘mwah’ sound that Rio would have thought Agatha would hate but she didn’t respond at all.

Ralph then turned and threw the rest of his wine down his throat, wincing ever so slightly and then turning to smile at Rio, back to his charming self.

“Nice to see you, Rio.”

Rio barely had a chance to wave before the man had turned on his heel and disappeared back into the house.

It was strange. Being suddenly confronted again with the person the subject of your months-long fascination had chosen to be with.

Because Rio wouldn’t have picked Ralph for Agatha.

She’d known that the first time she met him. She knew that now.

Sure, he was handsome, seemingly harmless though a bit obtuse, but there wasn’t much substance to him, no real personality past the cookie cutter mould he’d been carved out of.

But who was Rio to say it didn’t work. She’d been told for weeks now how ‘happily married’ Agatha was.

And maybe Agatha turned a blind eye to Ralph who sometimes looked at other women, maybe sometimes touched.

But all evidence pointed the way of a happy, functioning marriage: a cute, well-adjusted kid, a great house. What else was there?

And Rio, single and pining, was hardly a good judge of who was made for each other and who wasn’t.

So Agatha maybe flirted a little, she was a movie star, she was built to be charming to everyone. And Rio just so happened to be charmed by everything she did.

“He’s handsome. Very handsome.”

Agatha scoffed lightly and when Rio looked up from their joined hands she saw Agatha was looking at her.

“What?” Rio asked quietly, a small smile tugging at her lips, “You think just because I like girls I can’t recognise a handsome man?”

“No, I just…” Agatha sighed and Rio’s smile faded as she shifted in her seat to watch Agatha.

“What? Think I have bad taste?”

Agatha laughed and turned to Rio properly, her smile not quite reaching her eyes as she gazed across at her, “I don’t know anything about your taste.”

“It’s good,” Rio said, “I promise you that.”

Agatha opened her mouth to say something but closed it again almost as quickly and Rio wriggled her brows at her, attempting to get her eyes to light up again as they had on the basketball court.

“I’ll have to take your word for it.”

Agatha had whispered the words and Rio looked away suddenly for fear she’d see something in her gaze she’d never recover from. She felt dizzy with her need for Agatha, unsure how this had happened again when she’d entered the house so determined to keep a hold on herself and her emotions.

There was a beat.

A silence.

And then Rio squeezed Agatha’s hand, afterwards pulling her own away for fear she was overstepping.

Agatha allowed it but dropped her gaze to where Rio had placed her arm on the arm of the chair and offered suddenly: “You want to take a shower?”

“Oh? Do I smell?”

“No, I just-…”

And Rio looked up to meet blue eyes again and she bit down on her lip, watching as Agatha’s gaze flew briefly to her lower lip now pulled between her teeth.

It must have been a trick of the light, a misfire of her brain, because as soon as she thought she saw it, it was gone. Agatha’s gaze was back meeting her own and she was smiling slightly, “You’re maybe just a little sweatier than when you first arrived.”

“Just a little?”

Rio lifted her arm and made a show of smelling her armpit and Agatha laughed properly this time, and when Rio looked back at her she looked more relaxed.

But it lasted all of two seconds.

“Hon?”

Ralph had appeared back in the door, gazing over at his wife in a new clean, crisp outfit that looked very similar to the one he’d been wearing before.

Rio pulled her arm down quickly, a little mortified that she’d been caught out trying to impress his wife in the most juvenile way possible.

“My uber’s here. I’ll see you tomorrow?”

Rio felt her heart leap to her chest when Agatha stood from her seat and went to kiss Ralph’s cheek. And her treacherous brain told her that Agatha hadn’t kissed her like that. She’d been softer, lingering longer, had pulled back slower.

She dropped her gaze and reached for her wine.

She didn’t look up again until she heard Agatha sit down on the couch and even then she didn’t look Agatha’s way, just glancing up to where Ralph had previously been.

“Offer’s there,” Agatha said as if they hadn’t just been interrupted, “if you want to shower, you can.”

“I didn’t bring anything to change into,” Rio said, more shyly than she usually would and she caught Agatha’s gaze then, seeing her tongue dart out to wet her lips and feeling the dull blankness of her mind as she watched it retreat back into her mouth.

All the time. Constantly. Forever.

Rio nodded, suddenly feeling shy again and wondering whether this was a good idea.

Celtics colours.

Wine, she thought idly, but her gaze drifted across to Agatha and she wondered if she was another reason she felt breathless.

“Rio,” Agatha muttered quietly, and Rio turned to raise her brows at Agatha, challenging her to it.

“Mm?”

“I can kick you out, you know.”

“But you won’t,” Rio grinned, turning where she stood to lean her back on the counter again, and reaching across Agatha to get her wine.

Agatha only huffed but returned to her meal prep, occasionally adding to the conversation where Rio and Nicky mostly spoke about basketball and occasionally soccer.

By the time dinner was made, a prawn linguine, with chilli on the side so Nicky didn’t have to have it, and it was presented in a large bowl in the middle of the table in the breakfast nook, Rio had decided that Nicky was the best kid she’d ever met.

And Agatha, well she knew how she felt about Agatha.

And sitting here, at the little table with her son, half a bottle of wine in her system, and Agatha’s knee every so often knocking into her own, was enough to confirm it.

But Agatha’s touches were getting bolder, always hidden from Nicky’s sights.

The knee that had been previously just brushing her own was now pressed against it.

Her hand, when she placed her fork down and declared she was so full she couldn’t eat anything else, not even ice cream(!), had slipped below the table and was resting so her fingertips were on Rio’s thigh.

The pull of Agatha was too much to resist and Rio wondered if this was going where she hoped it might be.

But the presence of Nicky, the reminder that this was a family unit she were intruding on, made her hesitate with every return of Agatha’s touches.

Soon enough dinner was over and Agatha told Nicky he could put the dishes away tomorrow because his performance earlier had been so excellent and Rio was hovering by the island again, cradling her wine as Agatha wrapped up the leftovers when Nicky asked:

“Mom can we watch a movie?”

Rio raised a brow and smiled a little at Agatha who for a second looked disappointed and Rio wondered if she’d had other ideas in mind for what to do with their evening together but the question was soon thrown her way and Rio had no choice but to answer in the affirmative.

“I think you should ask our guest, don’t you?”

“Rio? I’ll let you pick.”

Rio laughed a little and turning her attention to Nicky again, she didn’t refuse.

So the little trio went to a room Agatha referred to as “the den” and Rio rolled her eyes at what was basically a library-cum-cinema room. Then again, twenty million a picture she supposed could buy whatever Agatha wanted.

Agatha came good on her promise of ice cream for Nicky and even brought a bowl for Rio, much to Rio’s secret delight.

And the three of them piled onto the huge, soft couch, with Agatha in the middle.

“Okay,” she said with a smirk, wriggling the control in Rio’s face, “What would Her Majesty like?”

Rio rolled her eyes, leaning across to place her wine down so she could tuck her legs back up and focus on her ice cream.

“Have you ever seen E.T., Nicky?”

“Of course he has,” Agatha said, her tone full of so much offence that Rio grinned at her.

“I love it,” Nicky piped up helpfully and Rio shrugged.

“Then E.T. it is.”

Agatha grumbled something about being called an “unfit mother” and Rio only laughed as she watched the large screen bring the movie up and the lights begin to dim.

“This place is ridiculous,” she whispered softly, shooting Agatha a look of immense amusement as she slipped down and slapped at Rio’s arm.

By the time the titles were done, Rio had finished her ice cream and placed the bowl quietly on the side, turning to see Nicky had finished his and was tucked under his mother’s arm.

The sight made her grin so much that Agatha caught her eye and raised a brow in question at Rio’s grin.

“Cute,” Rio breathed, motioning to Nicky before settling back down on the couch.

Ten minutes later and Rio’s attention on the movie waned somewhat as Agatha’s hand had moved on top of her own thigh.

Rio glanced down at it, seeing her fingers twitch towards her slightly and she felt a jolt in her stomach at the silent request.

Was it a request?

She couldn’t take her hand. Nicky would see. But Agatha wanted something and Rio thought about it for a second (actually a few minutes) before she casually placed her hand down on the couch between them, waiting patiently for Agatha to make her move.

She did, not two minutes later, placing her hand carefully beside Rio’s and turning it so just their knuckles could brush.

And Rio realised again then that all the months of second-guessing her own feelings, of being so sure about Agatha’s lack of, they’d all be wrong.

Agatha wanted this, wanted her.

And Rio couldn’t believe that she’d missed it, that she’d convinced herself of the old lie: “happily married”.

Because Agatha may have said it, but she’d been telling her all along that she wanted her.

She wanted, needed, Agatha to send Nicky to bed, so she would be able to turn to her and tell her she wanted her, that this was it.

But as the movie went on and their fingers continued to brush occasionally but never moved beyond it.

Rio knew that Agatha would have to be the one to make the move.

She couldn’t force it. Couldn’t make Agatha do something that she clearly wasn’t ready to commit to, maybe even to face about herself.

But it was okay, Rio thought with as much conviction as she had in her, because she could wait for her to be ready, and if it took longer, if it took forever, then so be it.

In years to come people could make a tragic movie about their lives and how their first kiss was their last kiss.

God, Rio thought suddenly, she was pathetic.

“Hey,” Agatha’s voice broke her from her spiralling thoughts of deathbed confessions and weeping at funerals and Rio turned sharply to look at Agatha, frowning a little in the darkness.

“Honey. There’s a pile of blankets below the table. Will you grab a couple?”

Rio nodded and reached down carefully to find what Agatha was talking about and pulled two blankets out. She held one in her lap as she leant across, blocking Agatha’s view briefly as she draped one over Nicky where he half lay against Agatha still.

He smiled at her and she smiled back, shooting Agatha a quick look before she settled back down and draped the other blanket over their laps.

Nothing happened for a while, Rio having already made the choice that death bed was the way to go. But then, she felt it, a gentle tug against the side of her thigh, a soft request for Rio’s hand below the blanket again.

Rio ignored it for a while because she had to temper the aching in her chest.

Agatha was right beside her, their shoulders almost touching, and now she was asking for her hand.

After a few seconds of not moving she felt Agatha’s touch relax against the fabric of her pants and then her hand moved away and Rio closed her eyes as she took a deep breath in, steadying herself before she did the inevitable.

She reached slowly beneath the blanket and found Agatha’s hand now back in her own lap and brushed her fingers subtly along the back of it.

From the corner of her eye she caught Agatha turn slightly to look at her but Rio was distracted by her hand moving back down with Rio’s silent request and as Rio cleared her throat - and old childhood belief that noise would distract from something only visual - she slipped her arm beneath Agatha’s and entwined their fingers.

Her chest flared with want but she fought it down and focused instead on what she did have, which was Agatha willingly holding her hand.

Agatha squeezed her in response and Rio shuffled until she was pressing as much of herself to Agatha as she dared with an awake Nicky so close.

If she could extract herself from her own body, walk in here and see the sight before her, she might think it were a little family, just having a casual movie night. She might think one of the woman looked so delighted to be there and the other looked calm.

Her gaze might fall to Nicky and she would consider him to be warm and comfortable and loved.

And she might even pine for what she was seeing, might even consider it to be out of her reach, might not even be able to recognise that whilst it may be something she couldn’t truly have, she could have it for tonight, and maybe that would be enough.

Rio held Agatha’s hand for the rest of the movie, and every so often Agatha squeezed her or brushed her thumb over the back of Rio’s hand, until the credits rolled and Agatha made a move to nudge a sleepy Nicky from where he’d tucked himself in.

“Bed time, I think.”

Nicky didn’t protest but Rio almost did because Agatha moving meant that she had to release her hold on her hand.

But she did and Agatha turned her hand over to squeeze her thigh before she pulled away entirely, whispering to Nicky as they both stood, “Say goodnight to Rio.”

Nicky smiled and leant in to hug Rio, and Rio readily returned it, giving him a gentle squeeze before releasing him back to Agatha.

“I’ll be right back.”

The One Rule

Chapter Summary

Rio breaks a rule.

Agatha breaks a lifestyle.

Chapter Notes

I’m posting this after editing with some (a lot) of wine in my system so I hope it’s acceptable to you all

See the end of the chapter for more notes

”I’ll be right back.”

Something in Agatha’s gaze made Rio suddenly feel nervous, as if she were suddenly expected to know what to do next, as if this whole thing hadn’t been confusing and painful but energising and exciting.

So Rio sat on the couch, toying with the blanket across her lap. She finished the now-warm wine that was in her glass and spent the rest of the time wondering what would happen when Agatha arrived back.

But she didn’t have to wait too long. Agatha was back within twenty minutes.

She paused in the door and asked: “Would you like more wine?”

“Please.”

So two more minutes later and Agatha was back beside her, pouring them both more wine before she turned to Rio properly, offering her glass back to her so they could cheers.

Their eyes met over the rim of the glasses and Rio felt her stomach flip because how had she missed it before? Agatha wasn’t looking at her any differently than she usually would. Only now, she knew what that look meant.

“Nicky’s keen for dinner dancing to be a thing now, I hope you know.”

Rio smiled a little, relaxing at the memory as she watched Agatha shift her weight, wrestle with the blankets below her until she could slip under them and Rio felt a rush of warmth as Agatha’s knees knocked hers lightly and she tried to play it cool by placing her elbow up on the back of the couch pretending none of this was affecting her.

But she wasn’t that good an actress.

Or maybe it was just affecting her that much.

“You’re welcome for that,” Rio managed to get out, choosing a good way through this was to drink more wine, so she did.

“Are you offering to come over every night for pre-dinner entertainment?”

Rio swallowed down the mouthful of wine thickly and watched Agatha’s gaze drop to where her throat bobbed.

“For you or Nicky?”

Agatha’s gaze snapped back up suddenly and Rio felt dizzy all of a sudden, because Agatha’s pupils were blown and her lips were parted and she’d moved a fraction of an inch closer, her knees now either side of Rio’s right knee on the couch.

“Both?” Agatha tried and Rio wondered if she were trying to rein it in again, trying to calm the rising tide of tension between them.

“I would if I could,” Rio said truthfully, trying to calm her heart from racing away with itself.

Agatha’s gaze had dropped again and she turned away slightly from Rio, and Rio knew her decision earlier had been right.

Agatha wasn’t ready.

She reached for her hand and tugged it until Agatha turned back to face her, a slight furrow in her brow as she did.

“I’m going to get an uber home. I don’t think I should stay tonight.”

“No,” Agatha said quickly, giving herself away in her urgency, “I’d like you to stay. Please?”

And Rio knew Agatha wouldn’t ask if she didn’t mean it so she nodded and squeezed Agatha’s hand gently, dropping her gaze to it.

“I was thinking about Friday dinner during the movie,” Agatha said slowly, clearly thinking her next words over cautiously, “Ralph will be at work until just before everyone arrives and Nicky will be away at a friend’s after school so maybe you could come over earlier?”

“I’m sorry,” Agatha said quickly, turning and wrestling with the blanket until she was out from under it.

In another world, Rio would be strong with it.

She’d take charge and win the war with her own feelings and tell Agatha that it was okay and that they were both a little drunk and that maybe playing happy families together for an evening was confusing for them both. And then she’d go home and they’d see each other at the next industry event.

“It’s okay.”

“It’s not,” Agatha snapped quickly, her words laced with a panic that Rio recognised as fear.

She reached for her slowly, just tentatively holding her arm.

Agatha didn’t move away.

“Agatha. Tell me how you’re feeling.”

Rio felt Agatha’s arm shift slightly as if she were to pull it away but a second later she was turning around and Rio’s heart stuttered in her chest at the sight of her soft expression, her gentle gaze.

“I don’t really want to talk.”

Rio could only nod, only watch Agatha with an equally gentle gaze though her fingers flexed on her arm and her body shifted a little closer.

Her mother’s empanadas and her own basketball jersey.

Sweet. Domestic.

Now a fantasy.

She’d been a fool to think it could be anything but.

Alice hadn’t been right that Agatha didn’t want her at all. But she had been right that if anything were to happen it would be a flash of desire, a quick fuck with no feelings and then nothing.

And Rio would be shunned because Agatha would make it so.

She’d push her from Hollywood because she could and because the fear of people knowing she’d stooped so low as to sleep with a barely-established actress like Rio would be enough to make her burn Rio’s career to the ground.

She could block her from the best producers, the best studios, the best directors.

“Rio?”

Alice asked suddenly, making Rio snap from her doom spiral.

“What? Sorry. I didn’t sleep great.”

“Well snap out of it. Tonight’s important to me. Agatha is Jen’s best friend and I know you two are getting on now but you need to nail this. Not just for me but for your career.”

Rio rolled her eyes but felt her stomach flip as she realised that her stupidity would impact Alice too.

If she were flung from Hollywood then Alice would be right behind her.

And what that meant for hers and Jen’s relationship, she didn’t know.

But Rio hadn’t spoken for a second or two and Alice was already filling the silence.

“Jen floated the idea of a joined project. Of something Agatha was producing. Just an idea still but I think if things keep going well then we might be in there.”

“As in… me and Agatha working together?”

“Yeah. I know she’s Agatha Harkness but you’re hot shit too. Don’t forget that. She’d be a fool to overlook you and the pull you have at the box office.”

Rio sighed and flopped down onto her floral bedspread, toying idly with the soft fabric by her hip.

“Besides in just a couple months time you’ll have an Oscar nomination and-…”

“Wait, wait. Alice.”

Rio took a deep breath and then fell onto her back, staring up at the ceiling as she said: “Has Agatha asked Jen about this? Has she given her some sort of-…”

“She’s optioning a movie and has you in mind for one of the roles, apparently. Don’t get your hopes up. It’s early days but just to say: keep on her good side. Being friendly with Agatha is your ticket to the best this town has to offer.”

Not long after, they hung up.

Rio had long since fallen into a deep depression, and she allowed herself to wallow in it for an hour only.

She timed it precisely. Keeping an eye on the clock on the side to make sure she didn’t slip into hour two of her self-pity party.

But her wallowing brought with it a determination to act, to protect, to reassure.

She couldn’t make Agatha want her. But she could protect Alice. She could ensure Agatha knew she’d protect her too.

And maybe, just maybe, Agatha wouldn’t destroy more than her heart.

Pushing her heartache to the side, Rio focused for the rest of the day on building herself back up to a facsimile of an actress with the world at her feet and the kind of happy-go-lucky attitude she used to carry with her like a permanent badge of pride.

She went to the local market to buy fresh flowers and organic wine. She picked out a dress that was casual enough for a dinner at a friend’s but pretty enough to still look like she’d made an effort. She put on a little more makeup than she usually would, wore more jewellery, wore flattering lipstick and nice shoes.

In short, she did everything she could to look good, so she’d feel good too.

When Alice was outside her door at six, honking impatiently, Rio felt more energised, more ready to face Agatha than she had felt since she received the text.

“Goddamn, Vidal.”

Rio slipped in the car beside Alice and narrowly avoided smacking herself in the face with large bouquet of flowers.

“Pulled out all the stops? Or just got a date after this?”

Rio smirked a little, pleased her choice to dress up had an immediate affect, even if Alice weren’t the intended audience.

“Just wanted to look good for our host.”

Not a lie.

Alice hummed and started the car back up as Rio looked her best friend over with a small smile.

“You look good, superstar. If I didn’t know any better I’d think you were trying to seduce your girlfriend.”

“I’m always trying to seduce Jen. By Sunday we’ll be away again so I need to squeeze in as much seduction as possible.”

“You can stay, you know? If it’s easier? I know you get so bored. And now you have Jen, well, it’s different.”

Alice shot Rio a sideways glance and Rio knew what she was about to say before she even said it: “You need me around. You get lonely.”

“I do not.”

Alice just raised her brows and Rio sighed and turned her head to look out the car window.

“It’s time to find someone.”

“Alice.”

“I mean it. You’re cute and funny and kind and rich and-…”

“Stop.”

“After the Oscar’s. Four more months. I want you to seriously consider getting out there. You’ve not had a proper girlfriend since college.”

“Not true. Victoria was-…”

“You saw her for six months then decided you weren’t in love.”

“And? Still a girlfriend.”

“It was an extended affair.”

Rio rolled her eyes, knowing Alice was right. Victoria had been a warm body who knew how Rio liked to be touched and how to make good coffee and where the best bars were in any city in the world.

But they hadn’t really talked. They hadn’t shared things or welcomed each other into one another’s lives.

It was just convenient. Just easier than having no one.

“Besides,” Alice was continuing, taking Rio’s silence as an invitation to go on.

“I want to see you happy. To see you settled.”

“Don’t lie. You think it’ll be good for the brand.”

“Don’t be a bitch. You’re my friend before you’re my client. I’ve not been this happy in a long time and that’s because of Jen. I want that for you too.”

Rio felt her chest constrict as she thought of what could have been with Agatha.

Was there a universe where Agatha had left Ralph and run away with Rio? Could she have seen herself as a step-mom to Nicky? Would they work longterm? Would Agatha get bored of her or decide a fleeting fantasy of Rio wasn’t as good as the reality?

But then a hand had reached across, and amidst the forest of fresh flowers, Alice had linked their fingers and was squeezing Rio firmly.

“I love you. I want you to be happy. You deserve someone who will make you happy.”

But Rio found she couldn’t respond.

She only squeezed Alice’s hand and tried to funnel into it the acknowledgement of her friend’s care.

They remained silent for the rest of the short journey into the Hills and by the time they arrived Rio had schooled her thoughts again to be ready to act rings around her own emotions.

They traipsed up to the gate and waited for the familiar sound of it unlocking, Rio watching Alice with amusement as she took everything in.

“Holy shit.”

Rio laughed even as the door opened and Agatha appeared in the doorway.

She was in a striped blue and white button down and matching white jeans. She had a pair of glasses on her head and a hardness to her expression that made Rio want to turn and run.

“Agatha!” Alice shouted with a grin, moving towards the woman with a beam and brandishing her wine, “this place is… huge.”

Agatha only smiled tightly, stepping aside to let Alice in and offering only a cursory hug as the smaller woman stepped inside and muttered another, “holy shit”, once she’d seen the inside of the house.

“Ralph and Jen are out back.”

“I’ll put this in the kitchen,” Alice said happily as she slowly stepped away and gazed all around her in awe of what money and taste could produce.

It was Rio’s turn to step up now and she did so with a fear that so clenched her heart she could barely breathe.

But Agatha hadn’t reached for her or even offered the small hug she’d deigned to give Alice.

Her blue eyes were focused on the floor and Rio sucked in a sharp breath at the sight of Agatha’s jaw flexing before her.

The jaw she’d brushed her lips and tongue and teeth across only two nights ago.

“Hi,” she offered softly, turning fully to Agatha in the open doorway, unsure whether or not ignoring her would be a better option.

“I thought it meant more than that,” Agatha said in a venomous whisper that chilled Rio’s very soul.

Agatha moved then, still not exactly looking at her as she made to close the door behind her and Rio had to shift quickly to avoid it closing on her.

“What?”

But Agatha raised her gaze to her and Rio was thunderstruck by what she saw in it.

Agatha looked hurt.

She looked devastated.

“Not glam enough for you? Not fun and sexy with a kid in tow and-…”

“Agatha.”

Rio felt a prickling sense of shame tickle her body, hitting every inch of her with it’s creeping tendrils and it’s insidious promise of pain.

“You called it off.”

But as soon as the words left her lips she could see in them a truth she’d missed before. Perhaps because she’d expected Agatha to call it off. Perhaps because she’d assumed she would or maybe, just maybe, she’d hoped that she’d do it sooner rather than later to save Rio falling more for her.

Agatha’s brows furrowed a little but she still looked just as hurt as before, her face just as taught.

They stared at each other for what felt like a lifetime, and Rio took a step closer even as Agatha took a step back, her body coming into contact with the closed front door behind her.

Agatha took a soft breath.

And Rio had never seen her eyes sparkle like that before.

But it wasn’t something she ever wanted to see again because Agatha was fighting tears.

“Ralph was here. I had meetings. I couldn’t get away and you couldn’t come to me.”

Oh.

Oh.

There was a noise then through in the kitchen that made Agatha’s gaze dart from Rio’s for the first time since she’d looked up, and Rio felt in the absence of it a sudden sinking feeling of panic overwhelm her.

Agatha hadn’t pulled away. Agatha had simply had to change plans.

But now Agatha was walking past her and Rio swallowed thickly where her perfume filled her lungs and she had to fight to remain cognisant of the role she had to play today.

It was different to the one she’d assumed it would be.

She wasn’t a spurned lover.

She was a grovelling one.

She turned to follow Agatha into the kitchen and found Ralph in there with her.

He looked handsome. And Rio felt sick that he was there. In his kitchen. Where he had every right to be when Rio was just there to make up the numbers, to keep Alice company.

He was opening a bottle of red and indulgently sniffing the cork. “Beautiful bouquet on this one.”

Agatha was fetching another glass before placing it on the side, glancing at Rio as she did.

She’d pulled back the tears that had threatened to spill but still looked haunted.

Rio’s nausea increased.

She forced herself to look away and swallowed the sickness down.

“Pinot isn’t for me. Tastes like juice. I prefer a Barolo. Fuller bodied,” Rio said in Ralph’s direction, even as her eyes moved back to Agatha as the woman moved forwards to take her flowers from her.

“Oh no, a Pinot Noir for me. Much lighter. That way you can enjoy the fruits.”

But Rio didn’t much care for Ralph’s opinion on wine, or anything at all for that matter.

Agatha’s hand had just grazed her own when she took the flowers from her and Rio felt her whole body react to it as if she had burned her with a lit match.

“Ralph,” Agatha said as she turned away from Rio, moving to a cabinet to fetch a vase.

“Enough wine talk. Go entertain our guests and top up their glasses. I’ll be out with Rio in a second.”

Ralph didn’t object to this but then Rio supposed he wouldn’t, would he? It was Agatha who was the catch here. Agatha with the millions and the face that could launch a thousand ships.

And Ralph was just a man.

Left alone again, Rio placed the tote bag with the bottle of wine she’d brought on the side and remained silent as she turned her gaze to Agatha who seemed intent on the flowers she was currently arranging.

“You thought I’d had my way with you and were done?”

 

There was a beat of silence and Rio felt the sickness settle in the base of her throat.

“Or maybe you thought I’d changed my mind? I’d faked it and lied to you?”

Agatha’s tone hadn’t softened as she transitioned from instructing Ralph to berating Rio and Rio flinched with it, moving slowly closer.

“I thought-…”

“You could have at least had the decency to tell me. To use your words, Rio. God knows you use them enough any other time. I am not some slut you fuck and then ignore.”

It would have been easier if Agatha had slapped her.

But she persevered, being braver now than she had been when she had assumed Agatha didn’t want her anymore.

She moved close, placing her hand on the island by Agatha’s hip and when she didn’t react or pull away she moved it to her body to get her to turn to her.

Agatha resisted for a second before she did, and Rio felt her heart thrum in her chest when she realised that Agatha wasn’t looking at her but her eyes had gone that same watery way again.

She raised her hand cautiously to cup Agatha’s cheek and lifted her head up to look at her properly.

It was dangerous. Too out in the open.

There would be no good excuse if anyone walked in.

But Rio didn’t care. And Agatha clearly didn’t either.

“I assumed you’d got what you wanted out of me and I didn’t know what to say. But I wanted to come here and let you know that even if that were true, that I’d never tell anyone what happened. You’d always be safe with me.”

“Don’t say things like that,” Agatha breathed softly, as she moved her hands to the collar of Rio’s dress.

“Why not?”

Agatha just shook her head and pulled away, her fingers tightening their hold and then releasing suddenly, and Rio felt like she’d faint as her own hand hovered in the space between them.

“We can’t do this. The other night was a mistake.”

“Agatha, don’t. Please.”

“I got carried away. I wasn’t thinking straight.”

Rio took a sharp breath in and reached back out for Agatha, this time stepping close so she could wrap an arm around her front and reach for her hip.

“Agatha.”

Agatha didn’t pull away, she simply remained standing, her gaze down on one of the daisies hanging limping from the bouquet. She touched it lightly as Rio’s fingers curled more tightly around her hip.

“Don’t.”

“It’s best for both of us,” Agatha said quietly, turning her head to look at Rio who was now just inches away.

And Rio knew she was right, knew she was doing to right thing. And that it was only Agatha who could decide. After all, it was her marriage.

But it hurt. It hurt beyond reason.

She met Agatha’s gaze and saw her blue irises begin to swirl again with unshed tears and she couldn’t believe it when she felt herself nod and pull away.

And Agatha opened her mouth as if to say something but Rio had turned away quickly for fear she’d fall to her knees and grovel if she didn’t.

She made quick strides towards the doors and didn’t turn back to see Agatha watching her.

Outside in the still warm September sun, Rio saw a discarded basketball on the deck and thought of the little boy who must have left it there.

She thought of his smile and his charm that was so like his mother’s.

And the evening she’d spent with both of them. Of the world now completely shut off from her grasp.

And then Ralph came into view, sitting in one of the armchairs and grinning across at Rio as she approached.

She’d been right the first time.

There was none of him in Nicky.

“There she is! Talking shop with my dear wife?”

“Something like that,” Rio said with a sweet smile, feeling the absence of the feel of Agatha against her never more than when she was in the presence of the husband.

“What took you so long?” Alice accused with a frown, her arm draped over Jen’s shoulders on the couch.

“I was helping with the flowers.”

“Jennifer,” Rio added with a smile as she went to sit by Alice’s side, leaving the second armchair free for Agatha.

“Vidal. Always a pleasure, never a chore.”

Rio laughed as she settled in, brushing her dress down over her legs and crossing them demurely.

It was easy to pretend. It was what she was good at.

“Trying to convince my client to star in some crappy chick flick with you?”

Rio raised her brows and tilted her head as Jen watched her suspiciously from the other end of the couch.

“I didn’t know that was an option for polite dinner party conversation. But I’ll be sure to bring it up.”

Jen scoffed and Alice nudged Rio gently even as she raised her brows down at her, wondering if this had anything to do with their phone conversation the previous day.

But Ralph had moved from his seat and was pouring Rio a wine without checking first that she wanted red when there was an open bottle of white that both Alice and Jen were drinking.

She thanked him anyway and took a sip of the Pinot Noir, a testament to her acting skills that she didn’t grimace at the thinness of it.

But she was distracted suddenly because Agatha was approaching, and she caught Rio’s eye.

Rio had to look away for fear she’d dissolve before her.

“Finally, the host!” Jen shouted with a grin, “took you long enough.”

“Actually I’m also the host,” Ralph said suddenly and Rio looked to Agatha’s reaction to this but saw she was too focused on Rio’s red wine, raising her brows at it.

“Sorry, Ralph. Of course. Just used to it being mostly Agatha, is all.”

Agatha had stood from her chair, pouring herself a glass of white before she went to take Rio’s wine without asking and swapped the glasses.

“Rio doesn’t like Pinot Noir.”

Everybody turned to stare at Agatha as Agatha made eyes at Ralph, taking her seat up again.

Rio blinked, her hand now curled around the cold cup of her new wine glass as she watched as Agatha took her seat and sipped at the deep burgundy liquid she’d just stolen away from Rio.

“She didn’t say no.”

Rio’s head snapped in the direction of Ralph and she saw his eyes flash, a challenge to his wife for showing him up. Perhaps also Jen’s dismissal of his position as host getting to him too.

“But she told you in the kitchen she didn’t like it.”

This was more than just about wine.

Rio shifted slightly in her seat and looked back to Agatha, willing her to look her way and drop it.

“It’s just never good enough, is it?”

Rio felt the wind change around them, saw the flash in Agatha’s eyes and the twitch of her fingers against the red of her glass.

Ralph was staring at his wife, his free hand in a fist at his side, his gaze as cold as the wine in Rio’s glass.

“I think we got off topic here,” Jen said suddenly, panic lacing her voice as she sat forward from Alice and cleared her throat.

“Come on! You’re the dream couple! Cute kid, amazing house, both hot. It’s just wine. And Ralph’s right, Agatha. Rio didn’t say no.”

Rio felt this was a little unfair, she’d barely had time to and was being polite either way. Then, she supposed, she wasn’t being exactly polite when she was negotiating an affair with Ralph’s wife not minutes ago in the kitchen.

“You know what?”

Ralph had said suddenly, turning to Rio, “You didn’t say no and you also didn’t say you wanted the white. So we’re all at fault here. Which do you want, Rio?”

Rio knew this was a power play, that he was trying to get her on side, to manipulate her into going for the first choice but even if Agatha had handed her a cup of poison she’d have picked Agatha’s offering over his any day.

“I was being polite before. I don’t like Pinot Noir. I never have. But this,” Rio held up the glass and glanced briefly to Agatha. “This I’d drink any day of the week. Gladly so.”

They locked eyes and Rio thought she saw a flicker of the anguish she’d seen before in Agatha.

But she looked away quickly, unwilling to let herself get sucked in again.

Ralph scoffed and muttered something under his breath that made the atmosphere crackle with something dark and incendiary.

Alice’s hand flew to Rio’s leg and she dug her nails into her, turning her body ever so slightly towards her as if there were something coiled nearby ready to spring and Rio hadn’t seen it yet but she was in the predator’s vision.

Rio glanced at her best friend, saw in her eyes the panic that had caused her to turn to her and raised her brows in question.

But it was clear she’d missed something. That she hadn’t heard what Ralph had said.

But everyone else had.

“Ralph,” Jen had said quietly, shifting her weight ever so slightly forwards.

But Rio looked to Agatha and saw that she looked beyond reason suddenly, beyond any placatory tone that Jen may have used onto try and calm Ralph.

“Get out.”

Rio shifted slightly, Alice’s grip on her upper thigh so tight she thought she’d rip her dress.

“What did you say?”

Rio asked suddenly, wanting to know why everyone was losing it. She dragged her gaze away from Agatha to look at Ralph who still looked furious but who wasn’t looking at anyone in particular, his gaze on the floor.

“Rio,” Alice warned quietly, but Ralph was already speaking again:

“I said: fucking flirt.”

Rio’s brows shot up her forehead and Agatha raised to her feet, repeating what she’d said earlier: “Get out.”

“Surely it’s enough to have your little fan club on set, on the red carpet, but not at my table, convincing my son to swap teams. Flirting with you so openly.”

Rio moved her hand to Alice’s still clutching at her thigh and she went to extricate it gently, and Alice allowed it.

Rio moved cautiously from her position on the couch to stand just behind Agatha and touched her forearm gently, curling her fingers slowly around it, her steady gaze on Ralph who’d turned to watch her move to his wife.

“Agatha, don’t.”

“You need to leave.”

Ralph didn’t move, his eyes briefly dropping to Rio’s hold on Agatha before he raised his gaze again and looked across at his wife.

He watched her for a second and Rio could only guess the coldness in Agatha’s eyes, but she remained where she was just behind her, her fingers tightening ever so slightly on Agatha’s arm.

“I’m not homophobic,” Ralph said suddenly, sounding an awful lot like a homophobic person might.

“I don’t care that you’re gay. Or that you clearly have a crush on my wife.”

His gaze dropped down to Rio’s hand on Agatha’s arm again and Rio briefly wondered if he knew the fingers now clutching his wife’s arm had been inside of her if he’d change his mind on not caring about her crush.

He seemed to think on it, and his shoulders dropped a little.

“I was just getting back at you with the wine for Nicky, that’s all. He hasn’t taken the jersey off since he got it.”

Rio raised her brows at this, wondering why he was so concerned about this when he’d barely acknowledged his son a couple days ago.

But Agatha beneath her hand was still tense and so Rio shoved down her instincts to tell this guy to fuck off and to be a better dad if someone who’d known his kid all of one day could overtake him in the rankings. She swallowed thickly and squeezed Agatha’s arm as she said: “It’s fine. I’ve been called worse.”

“And,” she started slowly as Agatha shifted, “I don’t have a crush on your wife. I actually find her very smug and annoying and,” she paused as she felt Agatha’s arm flex beneath her hand, making her second guess her choice but she had to say it, had to do it for the sake of keeping the peace as well as letting Agatha know she’d keep their tryst safe, “and she’s not my type at all.”

Rio could feel both Alice and Jen looking at her and she saw Ralph do the same, but the only reaction she really cared about was Agatha’s, though she only had the gentle second flex of her arm to go by.

“Well I’m sorry,” Ralph said a little stiffly, and Rio wondered whether he was simply uncomfortable with the conversation of a lesbian’s preferences in women, if he wanted to get back to drinking his disgusting wine, or if he wanted to be thought of as the host again, take back the power that Agatha had so swiftly gathered for herself.

Rio only nodded once, not offering her forgiveness back and squeezed Agatha’s arm gently before she returned to her seat.

Silence descended on the little group again as Rio watched Agatha sit down, her face as angry still as she’d ever seen it.

It was touching, really, a display of protectiveness she would never have expected from Agatha.

Especially not now.

Or maybe it was something else. A self-preservation. A defensiveness.

And she didn’t take her eyes off of her until Agatha looked back up to her and Rio lost her nerve and looked away.

“Anyway,” Jen said quickly, still sitting on the edge of the couch where Alice had now stolen Rio’s free hand and was holding it hidden down against her own hip, looking a little shell shocked.

“Rio. Details. Industry crushes. Go!”

Rio raised her brows at this and cleared her throat quietly, squeezing Alice’s hand reassuringly before stealing her own away again.

“Now that would be telling.”

“Oh come on,” Jen said with her own raised brows and a look that said to Rio: ‘please keep the conversation going’.

“Okay,” Rio relented, but only to get the conversation flowing again. She panicked and her mind went blank suddenly and she stared at Jen like she’d never been asked a question before in her life.

“Wanda,” Alice added quickly, nudging Rio’s thigh, “Wanda. You like Wanda.”

“Yes, but-…”

Rio cleared her throat quietly, realising there was no point protesting when she had to come up with a name anyway and Alice had just done that for her.

“Wanda. Right.”

“The redhead?” Ralph asked curiously and Rio turned to him and nodded, feeling suddenly a little disloyal to Wanda and a whole lot disloyal to Agatha.

Despite what they’d just agreed in the kitchen.

But Ralph looked totally at ease again as if he hadn’t just insulted his guest and pissed off his wife.

Which infuriated Rio.

“She’s cute,” Jen was saying, which meant Rio had a chance to glance at Agatha who looked as if she’d just swallowed a very large pill as she drank down the last of her wine.

“She’s maybe going to be the only nomination for A24 this year. Sad, really. They had so much promise and just fucked it on all their marketing. Though the movie wasn’t great either.”

Agatha was staring at the table between them.

“We’re negotiating a little Christmas movie at the minute. Some big names attached, actually. Calderu, Kaplan, Maximoff, it’s an ensemble.”

“Oh god,” Jen scrunched her face up but Rio missed it, her gaze on Agatha still.

“Not the cancer one?”

“That’s it!”

“Cancer at Christmas. It’s poignant.”

“It’s crap. They sent it to Agatha but I passed immediately. Who’s Rio playing? Not part of the family surely? They’re all white.”

Before Alice could answer Agatha spoke for the first time since her last attempt to get Ralph to leave and she said, “Excuse me, I’ll be right back.”

Rio met Agatha’s gaze for a split second before she’d turned and left.

Her anger had morphed into something else, something that made Rio shift in her seat.

There was a pause and then Ralph followed her down and Rio didn’t turn away until they’d both disappeared into the house.

“Jesus, Rio. Are you okay?”

Alice turned to her immediately and placed her hand on her leg over where she’d been holding her so tightly earlier.

“He gets wound up,” Jen said softly, looking over at Rio with a gentle frown, “they both do. I tell Agatha she just needs to have sex with him more and they’ll be fine.”

Rio wondered if Jen knew how much sex Agatha were actually having with her husband but felt it best to not broach the topic.

“I’m fine.”

“I’m telling you, usually if things like that happen she screams at him until she runs out of breath. It was impressive, how you handled her.”

“I didn’t ‘handle’ her. I just…”

But Rio wasn’t really sure what she did and so she went quiet and took a sip of her wine.

“How she’s married to him, I don’t know.” Alice said with a deep frown as she turned in the direction Agatha and Ralph had disappeared to.

Jen sighed quietly, “Look, if it works it works, okay? He’s usually away and so is she and… anyway, her and Nicky are very happy.”

‘Happily married’, Rio thought bitterly.

“I saw a photo of him on the wall,” Alice said absently, swirling her wine, her frown still across her features, “he doesn’t look like Ralph.”

“Are you suggesting Agatha had an affair?”

“No, just, I thought he looked like Rio, actually.”

Rio blinked across at Alice and stared at her for longer than would be considered polite.

“Pardon?”

“Well he’s got dark eyes and a goofy smile and big buck teeth.”

“I do not have big buck teeth.”

Alice ignored this.

“Plus he’s a little tan and I just thought… yeah, there’s Rio’s kid.”

“That is-…”

“Now you mention it, it’s not that crazy,” Jen said with a frown, staring into Rio’s face as if she were mapping out what features of hers Nicky had stolen.

“Actually, not at all. Sure he’s not yours and Agatha didn’t just steal him?”

“I-…”

But a sudden movement from down the way alerted them to Agatha marching back up to them and Rio forgot all about their conversation as she entered the little secluded veranda.

“Ralph’s taking a work call.”

Rio didn’t believe this, and neither did the other two if their expressions were anything to go by.

“Agatha,” Jen said with a smile, “we were just saying-…”

But she lost her train of thought as Agatha, instead of taking her chair back again, stood before Rio and hovered awkwardly there, earning a frown from Jen and raised brows from Rio.

“I’m sorry.”

Rio shook her head slightly, frowning up at Agatha who was almost leaning over her.

The look she’d noticed before hadn’t been sadness, it had been longing.

“It’s fine. He didn’t mean it.”

But Agatha pursed her lips and slowly pulled away, reaching to fill everyone’s glasses with the right wine.

Jen cleared her throat and started again: “Agatha, we were saying how much Nicky looks like Rio.”

A soft sound of glass on glass rang out as Agatha accidentally knocked the lip of the bottle on Rio’s wine glass.

“Well….”

“What do you mean ‘well’?”

Rio blinked across at Agatha and watched as she slowly turned to look up at her, “Well… he does.”

“What?”

Alice snorted beside her and Rio turned to slap her, “I’m sorry? Is everyone listening to themselves? Your son doesn’t look like me.”

“I mean, he does,” Jen said with an unhelpful grin.

“He does a little,” Agatha said with a smile that made Rio soften to it just a little, the memory of what Agatha had told her two nights ago making her chest suddenly feel warm.

“Big eyes, sallow skin, goofy teeth.”

“And since when have I had goofy teeth?”

Even Agatha laughed a little at this and despite Rio’s outrage, she couldn’t help but be pleased they were all laughing now, all at ease without Ralph there.

Prick.

Unwilling to give up until she saw that the clock had struck 11pm and she would feel Alice’s wrath in the morning if she slept in or was less than chirpy on their early flight, she’d simply disintegrated where she sat, sobbing for a lost shirt with little cowboys with their flying lassos on it.

And Alice wouldn’t understand because she hated the shirt.

And Alice wouldn’t understand that it wasn’t just the shirt she was crying over.

It turns out that a good way to get over heartbreak is to be so busy that you can barely think.

To think about how they’d left it.

About how unhappy Agatha was in her marriage.

About how badly she wanted to see her, talk to her, touch her.

Setlife was the same as it always was. Rio was number one on the call sheet and so had to set a precedent which meant no flirting with extras, being earlier than anyone else to the set, knowing all of her lines and marks off by heart.

Which meant that her days off were mostly spent sleeping.

She was horizontal almost every hour she could be.

And not in any fun way.

In fact, she’d not slept with anyone since Agatha. And a month of no sex was longer than Rio had ever gone before. But even if she had the time or the energy she wouldn’t be interested.

Why settle when she’d had the best?

Even Alice was worried for her.

Which was made ever so slightly easier because Rio hadn’t heard from Agatha since that last morning spent pressed together in her bedroom.

Any spare time she had she spent making sure to call her parents. Ever since she’d been embarrassed by the care package they’d sent to Alice she was now diligent about speaking to them every week.

And in all honesty, it made her feel better. It made her feel normal.

Only one night, about six weeks into the shoot, she’d plugged her headphones into her cell to make the call and she was chatting away about something a cousin of hers had done when her attention was stolen away by something else.

“…and I just said to your tía…”

Agatha had text her.

Rio had been so distracted by the name that appeared in the modal at the top of her screen as she’d idly being scrolling Instagram - and only vaguely listening to her mother - that she’d forgotten to read the message preview.

“…he’s just always been such a good boy, un ángel…”

Rio swallowed thickly, only now vaguely aware that in her little house in Delaware Anna Vidal was happily chatting into her phone thinking her beloved child was paying attention.

She flicked out of Instagram and clicked into WhatsApp.

There on the Home Screen, right at the top of the list of her chats with coworkers or old friends, was Agatha’s name, the message and a little green ‘1’.

“…I have no idea how he gets away with it now…”

Rio clicked into it to expand it properly.

Agatha Harkness: I thought you’d be pleased to know that I’m taking Nicky to his first Celtics game next weekend.

Rio stared at it.

“… if you were doing anything like this dios mío…”

Agatha had reached out. Agatha was telling her her plans. Agatha was going to be much closer to Rio in just over a week.

And Rio had learnt her lesson now.

She’d first not text Agatha back for three days and regretted it.

Then she’d not text her back at all and regretted that even more.

“… anyway, your father was saying that he once knew…”

Rio Vidal: Can I come?

“…that niña encantadora…”

7:36pm
Agatha Harkness: I’ll buy you a ticket.

Rio’s heart leapt in her chest and she stared at her phone, unsure what had just happened and knowing only that next weekend she’d be seeing Agatha again.

And that Agatha wanted her there.

She wanted to see her.

“…mija?”

Rio was too busy staring down at Agatha’s last text that her mum had to repeat herself three times before she heard her.

“God, mom. Sorry. I’m so tired. Can I call you back tomorrow?”

There was a beat of silence and then Anna Vidal said in a softer tone, “Are you eating well? Do you need me to send anything?”

“No, mom. I love you. I’ll call tomorrow.”

“Okay, mija. I love you too.”

Rio hung up with a click of the button on the wire and went right back to staring at her phone screen.

She went through all the possible response she could think of and eventually settled on:

7:41pm
Rio Vidal: In exchange I’ll buy you a jersey.

7:42pm
Agatha Harkness: What would John Smith say?

Rio grinned at her phone like she were fifteen and her crush were online.

Turns out six weeks thinking she was safe from Agatha’s gravitational pull were just a delusion.

She had her in her orbit.

She chewed on her lip and her thumbs danced over the keypad before she eventually tapped out:

7:44pm
Rio Vidal: Hard to know what imaginary men might say. But the very real Agatha Harkness should thank me.

It was pushing things towards flirty perhaps, but not overstepping so much that Agatha couldn’t either shut it down or pull it right back.

7:45pm
Agatha Harkness: I’ve booked you a suite at The Langham. Is that thanks enough?

Rio couldn’t believe it. She wanted to reach through the phone to get to Agatha.

To pull her through it and have her here with her.

But she tempered her thoughts with the reminder that this wasn’t a private trip.

That anywhere Agatha went - particularly a big basketball game - she would be photographed.

And more than that, her seven year old son would be there.

Both things meant no subtle touches, no sly hand holds, no yearning looks.

And Rio could handle it because they’d agreed: they’d made a mistake, made it now properly, and it wouldn’t happen again.

But she was fucked now.

For the rest of the week all she’d be able to think about was the fact that she’d soon be back in the presence of Agatha. Soon be able to talk to her, to see if she missed her, to see if she still wanted her.

7:52pm
Rio Vidal: I’ll let you know when I see you.

7:54pm
Agatha Harkness: Nicky’s excited already.

7:55pm
Rio Vidal: Are you?

Rio put her phone down then. Ripped her headphones from her ears. Buried her face in her hands.

 

She’d slipped up already.

She took long slow breaths and had to remind herself that she was talking to the woman who broke into her house, who touched her leg whilst sitting just feet away from her husband, who cheated with her not once, but twice.

It would be insane for Agatha to have bought her a ticket and a hotel suite and to not be excited.

But the question felt exposing anyway.

It felt incredibly vulnerable to ask.

She waited until she could catch her breath again before she checked her phone.

8:01pm
Agatha Harkness: I don’t care for basketball.

Rio had to roll her eyes, had to huff a little at the response. Because surely Agatha knew what she’d been asking.

With Agatha’s refusal to play ball she pushed a little, because she couldn’t help it now, deciding that she could no longer run anymore. She couldn’t just lay down and let Agatha fuck her physically and emotionally.

8:03pm
Rio Vidal: I’m excited to see you.

Rio didn’t receive a text back after that. Not for five minutes. Not for ten. Not for twenty or even an hour.

She’d moved on, she had to. She’d gone to cleanse her face and get ready for bed.

She’d pulled her script out of her bag and was settling down for the night to force the lines into her Agatha-centric brain when the next text came through.

9:17pm
Agatha Harkness: We’ll see you Saturday at the hotel. Reception will have my room under John Smith. I’ll let them know you’re coming so you can come find us. Have a good week. X

Rio read and reread the message.

She read it so many times she memorised it like it were one of her lines that she was yet to even partially commit to memory.

She read it in her own voice, in Agatha’s voice, in the voice she hoped Agatha would use when she said it.

She felt the whispered words on her temple, on her cheek, on her lips, she felt it against her breast, over her ribs, between her thighs.

She didn’t respond to it. Not out of habit but out of necessity. She couldn’t respond to something that she didn’t know how to.

She put her phone down on the side and returned to her script.

The words were ephemera to her. The meaning behind them lost on her as she tried to focus in.

By 11pm she gave up. Deciding a quick run through in the makeup chair with Alice would be the best bet.

Sleep eluded her too.

She glanced up and shared a soft smile with her before she focused back in on the script.

She had just over two hours before she was due to shoot her first scene. Which was usually more than enough time to get lines into her brain.

“Amply sufficient,” her dad would have called it.

By some miracle, the time taken was enough for her.

She managed to squeeze the lines into her full brain and by the time she was on her mark she was Rio Vidal the actress again, not Rio Vidal the lovelorn.

The day went smoothly after that, with the only interruptions being from Alice telling her about some interview she had lined up later that evening over the phone.

And soon Agatha was pushed to the back of Rio’s mind, protected under lock and key so Rio could focus on being a person again.

Someone who took charge of the set and its culture with a gentle hand and genuine enthusiasm for what they were doing.

Or John Smith, as she’d labelled herself.

It was pointless to pretend she didn’t want to look good for Agatha.

“Someone’s coming,” Agatha said and Rio could hear the panic in her voice and it broke her heart as that coupled with Nicky’s firm grip on her arm made her sick with emotions she didn’t have the desire to name.

“He’s fine, Agatha. I’m just being cautious,” she said in soft English, now more worried about reassuring Agatha than being overheard.

“Can you stay on until they’re with you?”

“Yes.”

“Are you getting mobbed?”

“Something like that.”

There was silence for a while as nothing much happened. But Rio began to relax a little and she hoped Agatha were too.

“Any pretty girls?”

Rio raised her brows and bit her lip, glancing to the side to check that though people were looking they weren’t close enough to overhear her.

“Some.”

Rio felt Nicky toying with the fabric of her shirt and she glanced down at him, unable to see his face because of the angle. She gave him a gentle squeeze and he rocked his head back to look up at Rio and Rio grinned down at him matching his goofy smile.

“He’s quite the helper when it comes to-…”

“Don’t even say it.”

Rio laughed softly and turned when she felt a tap on the shoulder and a man in a Celtics bib was smiling at her.

“They’re here,” she said into the phone.

“Hurry back.”

Rio hung up and placed her phone in her pocket as she spoke to the attendant in a low tone, her hold never relenting on Nicky, even as the attendant moved them away to a separate area and stayed close as he spoke to his colleagues through a radio.

“Hi.”

“Hey! We couldn’t find you for ages but we just had to say hi.”

“Hi,” Rio repeated, feeling Nicky toy with her shirt again. She cleared her throat and looked across the way to see if their food and drinks had arrived yet.

“We were wondering,” one of them started as the other clocked Nicky and made to lift his cap.

“Woah,” Rio said quickly, pushing her hand away as she pulled him back.

“Everything okay, Miss Vidal?”

Rio glanced at the attendant and then frowned back at the women, her other arm now crossing over Nicky too.

“Fine. Don’t touch my kid.”

The woman who’d done it just blinked and at least had the decency to flush at Rio’s sudden change in demeanour, apparently recognising that she’d overstepped.

Rio turned then, once sure no one would be trying to get to Nicky again, and asked the attendant if he wouldn’t mind bringing the food and drinks down to them and then gently guided Nicky back through the crowds and out to the stadium.

Only when at the top of the tunnel to get to their seats did Rio breathe again and she released Nicky’s hand to let him run to his mum and dive at her.

Even from afar she could see that Agatha looked relieved to have him back with her and Rio knew she couldn’t look as stressed as she felt so Agatha wouldn’t panic more so she schooled her face into a smile and took her seat back up.

Agatha hummed, too busy kissing a wriggling Nicky on the cheek over and over to respond to the prospect of a stadium-cooked hotdog.

“Are you going to be loud?”

“Yes. I like to cheer my team on.”

“By the pitch,” Agatha instructed as if it were the most casual thing in the world and she motioned for them both to go.

“Court,” Rio corrected with a genuinely soft smile as Agatha rolled her eyes. But she stood all the same and held her hand out to Nicky to pull him with her. She stood with him just on the edge of the court, holding his shoulders as she bent down to grin at the camera with him, both in their matching caps.

Agatha took a few snaps and laughed when Rio flipped both their caps to sit backwards on their heads and Nicky giggled as the picture was taken.

And Rio couldn’t help but beam up at Agatha, watching her as she checked the pictures she’d taken and moving to look over her shoulder at them. Her perfume filled her lungs and she had to step back, feeling dizzy with it suddenly.

A voice behind her saved her from her sudden turn and she looked to see the guy who’d come to rescue them standing with a large tray with their food and drink.

“Oh god, thank you.” She moved quickly forwards and helped him put it all down.

“Want me to take a picture of the three of you? I’ll get good angles, I promise.”

“I’d love that,” Agatha said from where she was now beside Rio suddenly, “thank you.”

“Caps forwards? Caps back?” She asked with an attempt to pretend her stomach wasn’t doing flips at the prospect of being photographed with Agatha and Nicky. On Agatha’s phone. In front of thousands of people.

Nicky had fallen easily into place in front of his mum and Agatha’s hands were on his shoulders so Rio had to squash in.

“Better,” Agatha muttered softly and Rio cleared her throat before she finally relaxed into it, curling her fingers properly around Agatha’s shoulder and turning to smile for the camera.

She was aware behind their photographer that a lot of the crowd were snapping shots too and she whispered, “Jen will be furious.”

“So let her be.”

Rio raised her brows and watched in surprise as Agatha turned to smile at her, raising her chin slightly in challenge. “What?”

“Nothing. Just… missing something.”

“And what might-…?”

But Rio had transferred her cap to Agatha’s head and was grinning at the sight.

“Perfect.”

She ruffled her own hair to make sure it was sitting okay and turned sharply to smile for the camera again, squeezing Agatha’s shoulder as she did.

“One with the two of them,” Rio said after a few more seconds of posing. She stole her cap back and replaced it on her head and strode away, turning to admire the view instead of the most beautiful woman in the stadium and her son.

Shit.

She was in love.

She’d been in the precipice of it for so long that she hadn’t even noticed that she’d tipped over.

That she’d fallen head first and hadn’t even noticed until she was swimming in her love for Agatha, drowning in it, and swallowing it down like the cool beer in her hand.

She’d downed half of it before she knew what she’d done.

“No. Mama dances.”

“Oh does she?”

“You dance like that? Nicky says you do.”

“I think you know that isn’t true.”

“I don’t know,” Rio said with a smirk, “You have rhythm.”

Whether real or imaginary, Agatha blushed a little and Rio grinned at the sight of it, thrilled then that Agatha’s eyes dropped to it and she felt a little more of that hope that still stoked flames in her stomach.

She stood quickly and gave the cheerleader a quick, one-armed hug.

“Who’s this little guy?” The woman pulled half back, their arms still around each other as Rio swung to look where she was pointing and saw Nicky look suddenly shy again.

“This is Nicky. He’s new to the Celtics family.”
