“Hi,” Agatha said quickly, placing a reassuring hand on Nicky’s back before the cheerleader could address him.

“Rio, why don’t you introduce us?”

Bitch. Rio thought suddenly, wondering briefly if she had a tell for not knowing someone’s name and how she could get Agatha to tell her what it was.

“Of course,” she said quickly, unable to think of anything else to say and simply offering her free hand to refer to Nicky and Agatha in turn.

Suddenly she was aware of the crowd around them, of the people taking photos and videos and she wondered if she would come out well from this or if she’d tank her career because of a brief dalliance with a cheerleader two years ago and her love for the woman in front of her.

“This is Nicky. And this is Agatha.”

God, fuck me. Kill me. Now.

Agatha was looking at Rio now, her brows raised, her jaw tight.

And Rio felt two things at once: how cruel it was that Agatha was doing this to her and how good it felt that she was doing this to her.

Because it meant she was jealous. Surely it meant she was jealous.
Nicky, shy as he was, held his hand out and Rio forgot her torment for a second and smiled down at him.

“Please to meet you, little one. I’m Danielle.”

Thank fuck, Rio thought.

Nicky shook the woman’s hand and Rio moved away from her, withdrawing her arm from around her waist and turning to her properly.

“Think you could get us in with the players?”

“Babe, I’m barely allowed to be here for as long as I’ve been.”

And the lights moved and changed and Phil Collins began blasting signally the team’s imminent arrival so Rio and Danielle looked around them before their eyes met again.

“Leave it with me.”

Rio grinned genuinely at the woman and settled back down in her seat, her excitement overwhelming her previous concerns as she turned to Nicky to shake his shoulder but she saw Agatha’s hand already curled around it and her expression tense but purposefully softened for the lens she knew would be on them.

“She’s pretty.”

Rio’s brows raised from Nicky to Agatha and she tilted her head a little, her tongue poking in the side of her cheek.

“Old friend,” she said enigmatically and caught the flash in Agatha’s eyes.

The crowd roared into life around them and even the promise of her precious Celtics couldn’t tear her away from blue eyes.

But Nicky was on his feet and almost spilling his soda and so Rio had to shift her focus to the little boy as Agatha did too. And silently, without acknowledgement, they put everything aside to focus on making sure Agatha’s son had the best time of his life.

Rio took it upon herself to become the pseudo commentator for the little boy, making sure he knew who everyone was, what the plays were, why things were fouls and why other things were not fouls (“biased ref, hates the C’s”).

And Agatha spent half the time watching Nicky too, holding the back of his oversized jersey when he stood on his seat for a better view, and otherwise shooting glances at Rio as she dedicated her time teaching and entertaining her son.

By the time half-time was called Rio was exhausted from imparting her knowledge and screaming at the court.

Nicky was high as a kite on the excitement of the thing and due to the excess soda he’d consumed.

And Agatha was, and looked, more relaxed than she had in a long while.

Even as the boards began to light up and cameras headed their way she didn’t seem concerned or fussed at all as the spotlight first fell to her.

And Rio looked up at the jumbotron with a grin, beaming at the sight of Agatha’s smiling face on it. The crowds went wild for her. And she could see why.

Agatha Harkness sporting their team’s jersey was a win even if you weren’t a huge fan.

But the camera moved and suddenly Rio was on the board. She was a known fan. A known frequenter of games. So this was perhaps less exciting for everyone but she still received a huge cheer from the crowd as she waved and gestured for them to get louder for her.

And they sure did.

Nicky was giggling by her side and when the camera was away again Rio turned to stick her tongue out at him before she looked across at Agatha and raised her brows, “Oh Jen’s gonna be maaaaad.”

“Screw Jen.”

Rio laughed and reached down for her now warm beer, and finished it in one go, relaxing back in her seat as she luxuriated in the day out and vacation from her recent working life where she’d barely had time to think, let alone enjoy.

And then there was the happy kid bouncing to the music beside her and the woman beyond him, pulling him in to cuddle him into her side and ask him questions about the game.

Rio looked around at them and felt herself yearn once more.

The way Agatha was softer for Nicky, the way she sometimes was with Rio.

The way her hands brushed the soft hair sitting along his upper back, the hands that had done that to Rio, the hands that had held her own and caressed her cheek.

Agatha looked up then, her chin rested on Nicky’s head as he settled against her and she smiled curiously across at Rio, watching her watch them for a while before she shouted above the noise.

“Are you having fun?”

“Like you wouldn’t believe.”

Agatha laughed and then turned her head to kiss the top of Nicky’s and the game started again.

Rio resumed her new favourite role of Nicky’s personal entertainer and lifted him from his seat when the final whistle blew and their team won.

Nicky tried his best to give Rio tinnitus by screaming loudly by her ear but Rio didn’t mind because she too was bellowing her pleasure at the court.

Agatha didn’t shout but at least stood and clapped and soon moved closer to place her hands on both of their backs.

“Did you win?”

“Shut up!” Rio laughed, placing Nicky back on his feet again so she wouldn’t lose her hearing and her ability to stand straight for the next week.

“You know we did.”

Nicky was beaming so much that Rio worried he might actually break his face and then she saw it. He put his tongue between his teeth and giggled as Agatha took him into her arms and something triggered in her brain that she hadn’t noticed before.

They did look similar.

Her face fell slightly as she stared at him and Agatha caught it, and tugged at her shirt, making her eyes dart over.

“What’s wrong?”

Nicky was looking around and he turned serious again, frowning where Rio must look stricken.

“Nothing, nothing.”

Rio cleared her throat and tried to shake it off. Maybe it was a trick of the light. Maybe it was an overspill from her desire to be with Agatha.

Of her love for Agatha.

Regardless, it didn’t mean anything.

“We should wait a little,” Agatha was saying quietly, “just so the crowds are a little less. That security guard will be there when we get out the stadium but best just wait.”

Rio only nodded and lifted her cap to shake out her hair, and her attention was caught as she did as the cheerleader from before ran over and straight into her arms.

Releasing a soft noise when their bodies collided, Rio cleared her throat quietly.

“I had a word. Do you want to come back? You can wait in the tunnel when the guys come out the locker room.”

“Oh my god,” Rio babbled, unaware her hand was being held and blue eyes were down on it.

“Seriously?”

“Yeah!”

“Nicky?” Rio turned to Agatha and Nicky and saw the little boy hiding half against his mum now, blinking up at the cheerleader shyly.

“Want to come meet the team?”

“No thank you.”

“No?” Rio asked with a frown and dropped down to crouch before him, tweaking his cap up a little so she could see his face better, “Are you sure?”

Agatha bent down too, turning Nicky so the three now sat in a triangle, all the same level, all facing each other, Rio and Agatha knocking knees.

“Yes, mama.”

“Okay, honey. Why don’t we go back to the hotel and order some chicken nuggets instead?”

Nicky smiled at this and nodded furiously which made Rio’s concerns fade quickly but Agatha had taken her knee just as she’d made to stand again.

“You can stay with your friend if you want.”

“No,” Rio frowned, “no. I’ll come with you.”

Agatha only nodded and dropped her hold on Rio’s knee as they both straightened and Rio turned to break the news to Danielle.

“Maybe another time?”

“You have my number. Maybe use it sometime?”

Rio received a kiss on the cheek and the woman was gone, leaving only the three of them now by the edge of the court and Agatha avoiding her eye.

“A friend,” she repeated with raised brows even as she looked anywhere but at Rio.

“Yes. A pretty one.”

Agatha looked around then and Rio smiled a little at the intensity of her expression but didn’t push it.

Soon enough the attendant was back with them and as the stragglers left the stadium, so did they. Rio hung back a little to keep an eye on Agatha and Nicky from behind, intent on making sure there were no surprise fan interactions that would ruin the rest of their day.

They moved through the whispered sounds of their names and the unsubtle pictures being taken without much hassle and when they finally cracked the outer shell of the stadium and hit the cool outside air they were guided back to the waiting car with security in tow - which made Rio feel a hell of a lot better.

Nicky slid in first this time with Agatha in the middle and Rio bringing up the rear.

She felt the press of Agatha’s thigh against hers before she’d even properly settled in her seat and in the pretext of putting on her seatbelt she brushed her hand over the small of Agatha’s back, enjoying for a second the secret proximity to the woman she’d hopelessly fallen for.

By the time they were bundled back into Agatha’s suite, Rio was exhausted with the energy of the day.

She was left to lounge whilst Nicky went find something in his room and Agatha went to see he was fine before she came back out and sat by Rio’s hip on the couch.

“You’re so good with him.”

“He’s easy to be around.”

“What happened in line for food?”

“Nothing.”

“You wouldn’t have-…”

Rio sighed and sat slowly, now sitting level with Agatha on the couch and reaching to hold her wrist gently, as if that would help calm her.

“If I hadn’t had Nicky with me it would have been fine, and it was. I… I just wanted someone there. Just in case. I didn’t want him to freak out.”

Agatha’s jaw was working, flexing and unflexing with every clench of her teeth but her eyes were still soft and she nodded slowly, dropping her gaze to where Rio held her wrist.

“He’s shy.”

“I know.”

“You did the right thing. I shouldn’t have sent him with you in the first place.”

“Why did you?”

But Rio knew why. Agatha had thought with Nicky there Rio wouldn’t flirt. Would be too distracted. And she was right, obviously. But she didn’t know that Rio wasn’t interested in flirting with anyone anymore.

Anyone that wasn’t Agatha, anyway.

But Agatha didn’t respond and instead squeezed Rio’s hand gently before she stood from the couch.

“I’ll order food.”

Rio watched her go and then watched Nicky arrive back in the room holding up a mini basketball.

“Can we play?”

Rio laughed and glanced at Agatha who had pursed her lips in response, clearly not keen on the idea of her son and Rio smashed expensive vases in an expensive suite.

“Not tonight, buddy. But next time, okay? We gotta get you good enough to be captain of the Celtics!”

The little boy only nodded and jumped up on the couch beside her, throwing the ball up in the air to catch and soon they’d devised a game whereby they sat at opposite ends and gently tossed the ball back and forth.

Which Agatha only allowed because they’d get to fumble it and even when Nicky’s aim was off Rio could reach out to catch it before it drifted off to cause any permanent damage.

They evening went by happily, with Nicky entertained by Rio’s post-match analysis and thoughts on how she’d have done things differently and scored at least ten more points.

And Agatha contributed only to ask questions that would make Nicky laugh and Rio roll her eyes.

They feasted on nuggets and pizza and Nicky even got a special bowl of chocolate ice cream delivered and soon enough they lounged all on the same couch, with Agatha’s arm casually draped over Rio’s thigh and a tired little boy tucked into her side, unaware of his mother’s hold on the woman the other side of her.

The whole time Rio felt like she was flying.

She had Agatha back.

Nicky liked her.

Nicky wanted to talk to her or keep her talking.

And Agatha was smiling or laughing or rolling her eyes.

It was a facsimile of a family again. And Rio wanted it to last forever.

But Nicky had to be taken to bed and the illusion dissolved as the reality of being alone with Agatha meant she had to be brave, be bold, be as clear as she could be about how she felt about her.

Nicky gave her a quick hug and then Agatha whispered, “I’ll be right back.”

And she was alone, waiting for the woman she loved to come back to her.

Don’t Say It

Chapter Summary

Rio and Agatha talk.

Chapter Notes

Quite the sea change from the previous chapter! Be warned!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio sat in the familiar position on Agatha Harkness’s couch, albeit in an unfamiliar hotel suite, waiting on Agatha to return to her from putting Nicky to bed.

Unlike before she knew what was to happen when she came back to her because she was going to take control.

She had to.

She was going to come clean, to tell Agatha that it was more than the crush Alice had told her about, it was more than incredible sex and a lust so undeniable she felt like she was on fire whenever Agatha touched her.

She’d never been the first to say it, never been the first to feel it, but now, now she’d gone and fallen for the most famous woman in the world who just happened to be married, who just so happened to want her too. Maybe just not love her.

And maybe Agatha would pull away again, she thought, or maybe it would go how she hoped.

Agatha would tell her she was divorcing Ralph, that she was going to run away with her, that they could buy a cottage somewhere in the woods and live a happy and easy life just the three of them.

Just as Rio were imagining a forest-themed basketball court, Agatha appeared again.

“Hey, he okay?”

“Fast asleep,” Agatha said with a small smile, eyeing the dishes Rio had piled up on the side.

“You’re a good house guest.”

“I try.”

“Wine?”

Rio nodded with a smile and reached to hold her glass for Agatha when she came to pour the rest of the wine they’d started earlier.

The bottle was finished by the time Agatha filled her own glass and Rio pulled her legs beneath her as they leant to cheers.

“To an incredible win today.”

“To you making Nicky’s day.”

Rio paused before she drank and began to second guess herself once more. If Agatha did pull away then she’d take Nicky with her too and as much as she barely knew the kid she’d grown fond of him.

Or maybe everything Agatha had told her about the reason for his existence, the fact even she could now see they looked alike, his shitty dad, it was all making Rio feel protective of him.

Rio drank down more than a mouthful of the wine and noticed Agatha watching her carefully. But she’d turned away, glancing briefly in the direction of Nicky’s door, just taking a second to breathe.

She felt a shift beside her and a hand on her cheek and Agatha was turning her head to kiss her.

And Rio could have cried for it, could have suffered a thousand humiliations to just feel the way she currently felt with Agatha leaning into her, holding her in place so their lips could be together for the first time in over a month.

But it lasted barely five seconds and Agatha was talking again, her thumb tracing the familiar sweep over her cheek.

“It’s been too long.”

Rio reacted only by lifting her hand to curl around the thin fabric at the neck of Agatha’s new jersey and she swallowed before she whispered, “We need to talk.”

Agatha pulled away then and broke Rio’s hold on her as she put at least two feet of distance between them, her blue eyes over on the bar.

“Agatha,” Rio said softly, frowning at the reaction, unable to reach back out for fear she’d be rejected again.

“More wine?”

Agatha asked suddenly, pushing herself up from the sofa and grabbing her glass to march to the bar at the end of the room.

Rio watched silently, her traitorous heart thrumming in her chest as her eyes scanned over Agatha as she sourced a bottle from the fridge and proceeded to open it with an expert flourish.

“You never did tell me why the four.”

Rio blinked, her mind so cloudly she couldn’t determine the question.

“What?”

Agatha turned over her shoulder as she tugged the cork from the bottle with a soft pop. “My shirt.”

Rio’s gaze dropped to the large ‘4’ displayed on Agatha’s front and she felt herself blush for it.

“It’s just a number.”

“Then why react this way every time I ask.”

Rio bit down on the inside of her cheek, knowing Agatha well enough now to know she wouldn’t drop it.

“It was a random number, or was supposed to be. I knew the player’s wouldn’t mean anything to you so I was just trying to come up with a number and,” she shrugged and watched as Agatha slowly walked back to where she sat on the couch, stopping just before her with a bottle in one hand and her glass in the other, “you have four little freckles on your nose. Tiny ones. I only noticed them the last time we-… anyway they’re in a vertical line and they’re… whatever… four.”

Agatha didn’t react for a second and Rio feared she might laugh but she maintained eye contact and refused to look away. If she backed down now, she’d never get through the night.

The woman before her slowly came back to life, stepping past her and sitting down beside her.

“Drink your wine,” she said in a soft voice, her gaze elsewhere as she lifted her own glass to drink down the remnants of the wine there.

Rio did as she was told and winced slightly at the volume of the liquid that poured down her throat.

But Agatha was soon filling her glass back up with the new wine and their eyes met again. She looked softer again, far more at ease than she had been when Rio had suggested they talk.

And Rio had to look away for fear if Agatha kissed her again she’d forget about talking altogether.

“Have things,” Rio started slowly, knowing she needed to get to the point quickly or she’d get drunk or too nervous and wouldn’t be able to get to what she knew she needed to bring up, “with Ralph, have they been… any better?”

“Ralph’s fine,” Agatha said curtly.

Rio turned to look at Agatha then and saw her focus in on her wine, saw the flex in her jaw.

“Agatha.”

Agatha glanced over and Rio almost lost her nerve entirely.

“Have you had sex with him since we were together?”

Agatha turned away again and took down another gulp of wine. Rio held her glass in her lap, one hand curled around the cup, the other toying with the stem.

“No.”

Rio could only nod, only breathe a silent sigh of relief that nobody had touched Agatha since she last had. Least of all Ralph.

The man who didn’t deserve her but had her all the same.

“Have you?”

Rio shook her head, watched Agatha eye her for a while and then turn away again.

“Why not?”

No one compares. I’ve barely had the energy to think because I’ve spent the last month learning lines and thinking about you. I just want you. All the time.

“Agatha,” Rio started softly, shifting where she sat to lean forwards a little but something sparked in the woman opposite and Agatha looked panicked suddenly, fearful.

“Don’t,” she said quickly, “don’t say something sweet. Not again.”

“Yeah. Tried to put them in a random order so some will be more tame than others. We’ll just point and shoot and edit out any that make you want to vomit.”

“Fine, I’ve a strong stomach.”

Rio was left alone then, perched on a small director’s chair in the middle of a blank backdrop, and she watched as everyone took their seats behind the camera and Alice’s smile returned to her face once she saw how Rio looked on the monitor.

She took it as a sign that she looked good.

“Ready when you are, Rio!”

Rio nodded and held her phone up to swipe up and read the first screenshot of a tweet.

She laughed. Genuinely. Loudly. And then looked to the camera with a raised brow.

“Hi I’m Rio Vidal and I’m here today with Buzzfeed to read thirst tweets.”

She dropped her gaze to the phone again and clicked her tongue. “God what a way to start.”

“@RidalsGal1 says: ‘I have two perfectly good holes and one needy mouth and none of them are full of @RioVidal. America please explain.’” Rio laughed again and looked at the camera.

“Jesus.”

She swiped the screen until the next tweet came up and whistled a low note as she read it over before voicing it: “@Darby789 says: ‘All I want for Christmas is for @RioVidal to use me as her personal’… oh my god,” she cleared her throat but her lips twitched into a crooked grin, partly for the camera and partly because she couldn’t believe what she was about to say: “‘use me as her personal cum bucket’.”

She ran a hand through her hair and looked up at the camera with raised brows, “Gimme a time and a place and I’ll be there.”

She heard Alice laugh and smirked as she looked to the next one: “@VidalsPlaything says @RioVidal I am free this Thursday for dinner and also anal thanks.’ Straight to the point. Like it.”

The next one she swiped to and laughed again, her tongue poking in her cheek as she chuckled and tried to get a grip on herself. “Jesus, man. You guys are freaks. Okay, @RioRioRio says: ‘Need @RioVidal biblically. Like, fist so far up my ass she’s wearing me like Kermit the Frog.’ Dios mío!”

She dropped the phone to her lap and looked back up to the camera, remembering the chat she’d had before with Alice and the producer; “make sure you comment briefly between each read”, “feel free to pause or laugh or whatever you need to do”, “try to react as naturally as possible”, “flirt, Rio. You’re excellent at it.”

“Listen, I’m pretty busy right now but I might have fisting time in the new year. I’ll keep you in mind.”

She looked back to the next one and smiled as she adjusted her free arm over her lap, “Okay this one is pretty sweet, actually. ‘@VidalsWife says ‘If I had one nickel for every time I’ve masturbated to thoughts of @RioVidal I’d be the richest woman in the world.’ Sweet. Romantic, even.”

She smirked at the camera and flicked to the next one.

“@Feral4Vidal says: ‘I love Rio Vidal’ and then it brackets it says… ‘I want Rio Vidal to rail me’.” She snickered and groaned as she grinned, “with all these requests I’m going to be a busy girl.”

And here is where she paused, when she swiped for her next tweet, and almost lost her composure. Because Agatha’s name was the first thing she saw.

“@HarknessHymen: ‘Feeling v French today. @RioVidal and #AgathaHarkness how would you feel about recreating the Eiffel Tower with me to celebrate?’” She forced a laugh, forced her smile to remain on her face. “I’ll text her later. Thanks for asking so politely.”

“Man, oh man, you people. I hope you don’t kiss your mothers with these mouths.”

She cleared her throat and shifted in her seat, beginning to toy with her hair as she read the next: “From @GayDream13 says ‘Sometimes Rio Vidal is so mommy and sometimes she’s so daddy I don’t know whether I want to suckle or suck.’” She laughed and took herself by surprise at it, blushing ever so slightly as she rocked her head back and grinned. “Christ.”

“Honestly this is the weirdest ego boost I’ve ever had.”

“@RiosToothGap says… oh god. They say: ‘I hope Rio knows she has an army of women willing to crawl miles over broken glass just to beg her to spit on them’.”

“I mean… how many miles, guys? Be specific please. Details.”

She looked up with a grin and saw Alice indicate one more and so she looked down to the next tweet on offer. And Agatha’s name was there again.

She cleared her throat quietly and read it over properly, feeling her jaw clench as each passing word made her feel increasingly more uncomfortable.

@Whre4Rio: I wouldn’t even want to join. I just want to live in a world where Rio Vidal knows what Agatha Harkness’s puss tastes like.

The recent flurry of internet interest in Agatha and Rio’s relationship that caught the attention of almost every journalist worth their salt. So Buzzfeed were clearly no different.

Most had focused on the rivals turned friends angle and some industry-focused journos had been deliberating and debating over whether this was a clever PR stunt for more attention, for more votes.

But Alice had told Rio that her Twitter was full of tweets like these and Rio was able to laugh most of them off, to roll her eyes and smile as Alice read them out, but sometimes they hit that little soft part of herself that wanted to cry instead of laugh.

She stared at it for a while and in her peripheral vision saw Alice moving a little as if to come to her. But she looked up before she could and shook her head slightly, “I’m sorry. Not this one. Can we cut that out and I’ll read one more.”

“Sure sure,” came the voice of the producer, keen to make sure Rio could continue comfortably and not ruin what he and his colleagues knew would be a huge hit for them on their YouTube channel. “Whatever you want. Start from the top on the next one.”

Rio smiled a little and swiped to get the next tweet up. She scanned it over and then looked to the camera with her smile back in place, “Everyone seems to think I wanna hurt people but I promise I’m actually every nice.”

She looked back at the tweet and read: “@D1ckD4re says ‘Rio Vidal could run me over, spit on my mangled body, and burn me to ash and I’d come back and thank her for it.’ I mean… I don’t want to do that but if you really want it then I guess who am I to say no?”

She laughed at her little joke, hamming it up for the camera to make up for her refusal to read the last tweet and then she dropped the phone and smiled, “Am I done humiliating myself now? Is everybody satisfied or would anyone like me to provide my services as a puppeteer?”

She held her hand up with a grin and wriggled her fingers, much to the delight of the video producers who now had their perfect end to an expertly performed video.

“We got it!” The main producer shouted and Rio raised her brows as Alice rushed in.

“You did? Need me to repeat or-…?”

“No, honest, Rio. You gave us everything we needed.”

Rio smiled and held the phone back out as she stood from her seat, “They were… Jesus.”

“Told you.”

“Hey. Amazing. Which did you skip?”

“Oh,” Rio shrugged and was grateful the phone was gone so Alice couldn’t make her show the tweet in question.

“Just one about… just felt a bit weird.”

“Okay. Well you fucking nailed it.”

“Yeah, yeah.”

“Must be all that sex you’ve not been having lately.”

Rio only hummed at Alice’s whispered words and moved with her to begin making the rounds, thanking everyone and saying their goodbyes and merry christmases as they finally, after a long day, left the little studio.

Outside by Rio’s old hybrid is where Alice pulled her best friend down into a tight hug.

“I’ll miss you.”

Rio sighed heavily and held Alice tightly against herself, turning her head after a few seconds to kiss her cheek.

“It’s just a few days.”

“Say it back, you bitch.”

Rio laughed and pulled away, “I’ll miss you too.”

Alice hummed and went to remove her bags from the back of Rio’s car, “You make sure your mom leaves me plenty of food, okay? Jen’s promised an anti inflammatory menu and… I think by the time I’m back I’ll be craving anything other than whatever that means.”

“Yeah, yeah, it’s practically a production factory in my poor little kitchen. I’ll try not to eat it all.”

“Very much appreciated,” Alice grinned as she shouldered her duffel and slammed the door shut.

Her expression softened as she took Rio in and Rio just knew she was about to ask her the same question she’d been asking her since she got back from Boston: “Anything you want to talk to me about?”

Rio knew she’d not kept her low moods hidden particularly well but she couldn’t reveal the truth for fear of outing Agatha so secrecy was important. It was paramount.

“No. Go and have a great time with your beautiful girlfriend and call me every day, okay?”

“Okay. I love you, idiot. Behave. Don’t run off on anymore trips that make my girlfriend furious.”

“Noted. I love you too.”

Rio left Alice to walk off towards the uber that had just arrived to take her to the airport and she felt her body shrink in on itself a little, feeling at ease now she was alone and had no secrets to keep.

The drive back to her home took less than an hour and she found herself singing along to random Christmas songs played by the local radio station.

They were cheesy but they were better than sitting in silence with her thoughts or scrolling through her podcast app trying to find something she could be bothered to focus on.

She slammed the car door shut and made her way into her home, the smell of fresh cooking filling her lungs as she closed the door behind her.

“¡Hola! Mamá, papá!”

A bag on the console table by the door caught her eye but she ignored it, assuming it was an old tote bag of hers and perhaps her mum had used it to go pick up some last minute groceries.

But what really surprised her was that no one had shouted back.

She dropped her keys into the little bowl on the side and slowly moved through the house, looking this way and that until her last resort was to head out to the back to see if they’d taken themselves out to enjoy wait remained of the December sun.

“Rio!”

Rio raised her brows when she came round the side of the house and saw her parents sitting on the little bench with two chairs she recognised from her dining room sitting opposite them and a blanket stolen from her bed lying on the floor before them with the remnants of what looked like a picnic.

“¿Qué pasó?”

Anna Vidal looked up with a wide smile where she sat beside her husband, cradling one of Rio’s large mugs in her hands.

“We had guests.”

“Guests?”

“Invitadas,” her dad confirmed with a wink.

Rio raised her brows as she surveyed the evidence of these guests. She sat in one of the seats as her mum offered an explanation.

“Your friend arrived with gifts an hour after you left with Alice.”

“Amiga bonita,” her dad added unhelpfully but Rio shot him a small smile, wracking her brains for who was in town and who might stop by the day before Christmas Eve.

Wanda?

“She had gifts and her son wanted to see you.”

Agatha.

“Mom, was it Agatha?”

Rio’s heart rate went through the roof and she wondered how long it would be before her Apple Watch buzzed and told her she was working out.

But her mum seemed to not notice and was taking a sip of tea before responding.

“Sí, sí, Agatha y Nicky.”

If Rio hadn’t been sitting she might have fainted.

“They…”

Her gaze dropped to the remnants of the picnic and she saw suddenly the telltale signs of a demolished plate of tostones along with guac and a bowl that definitely at some point earlier had had ice cream in it.

“You need to buy some furniture.”

“Mamá,” Rio insisted suddenly, keen to find out everything about how and why Agatha and Nicky had been in her house with her parents when she’d had no knowledge that they were even coming.

“How long did they stay?”

“¡Bah!” Anna exclaimed with a laugh and a wave of her hand, “Long enough to teach the little one how to make tostones and for your papá to bore Agatha to death with tales of your childhood.”

Rio felt sick again.

“Dad,” she said and turned to see her dad smiling at her and had to look away for fear she’d relent instead of remaining firm in her quest for details.

“So? What? Hours?”

“Sí.”

Rio ran a hand through her hair and cleared her throat.

“What’s wrong, mija? I’m sure if you called you could-…”

“How was she? Was she…?”

“Encantadora, educada, nerviosa.” Charming, polite, nervous.

“Nervous?”

“Ella se calmó.” She calmed down.

Rio nodded slowly and felt her father’s eyes on her even as she focused in on her mom.

“And Nicky?”

Anna looked to her husband and then turned back to Rio slowly, a small frown appearing on her face, “Él tiene tu cara.” He has your face.

“I know,” Rio said in a much softer tone than before.

“Was he okay?”

“Shy. He was looking for you.”

Rio could only nod, and took a second to process all this before she spoke again, “Did you like them?”

“Very much.”

“¿Quién no lo haría?” Who wouldn’t?

Rio smiled a little and dropped her gaze to a lone breadstick in a cup and took it.

“You’ll spoil dinner.”

“I’m starving.”

Really she just wanted something to do.

Anna hummed and Rio smiled as she took a big bite.

“You don’t want to look at your gifts?”

She almost choked.

“Gifts?” She spluttered, her dad moving to come around and smack her back to help.

“Gracias,” she mumbled as she cleared her throat loudly, “What g-…?”

But her mom had said Agatha had brought gifts and she almost choked again but this time on nothing. She stood and looked at her dad who was smiling warmly at her with raised brows and she caught something in his eye that told her everything she needed to know about what Miguel Vidal had guessed already.

“They’re under the tree,” her mom said with a wave of her hand and Rio nodded, turning back to shoot her a smile before she disappeared inside, moving so fast she was practically jogging.

Once back inside Rio took a deep breath and placed her hand over her heart to feel it thrumming it’s thumping rhythm against her ribcage.

Weeks and weeks of nothing and then this. Showing up to her house with gifts, with Nicky. Staying and chatting with her dad. Her mom taking the time to teach Nicky how to cook.

It didn’t make sense.

She moved to the tree and crouched beside it, immediately knowing the gifts that must be from Agatha.

Since childhood she’d had a bad habit of feeling and shaking her gifts, ripping them just enough to be able to see what she had before Christmas morning.

It was a habit her parents tried to shake her out of but one she’d never truly beaten.

And each gift dotted around the foot of the tree had small rips in them, evidence of Rio’s impatience.

Only two gifts at the front looked untouched.

And both had cards leaning against them.

Under no circumstances did Rio think she could wait two days to find out what they were so she picked the first card up and recognised immediately the handwriting of a seven year old.

Her name was written in large, wobbling letters and there was a small sticker of Santa in the corner that smiled dispassionately up at her.

She smiled back at it and then turned it over to open it.

Inside was a slim photograph rather than the card she was expecting.

She pulled it out front first and saw that it was the picture Agatha had taken of her and Nicky; the one where their caps were backwards and Nicky was grinning up at Rio who grinned back down at him.

It was shocking, really, how long it had taken Rio to see the resemblance. But it was there. As bright and obvious as the smiles on their faces.

She turned it over and with a pang saw that Nicky had written her a message and Rio hadn’t thought to send anything to him.

Dear Rio, wishing you a very happy Christmas and a happy new year. Go Celtics! Love, Nicky.

She saw beneath the boy’s wobbly handwriting the faint pencil marks that must have been Agatha’s, guiding her son’s message.

Turning it back over to see their smiling faces again she had to swallow down the guilt she felt that not only had Nicky written to her, he’d wanted to see her.

And she’d not sent him anything.

She placed the card aside and took up the gift she assumed was from him, unwrapping it uncharacteristically gingerly until she held a brand new Celtics scarf in her hands.

She laughed as she draped it around her neck and turned then to the next card.

God she hoped there wasn’t a photo of Agatha in there.

She wasn’t sure she could handle seeing that right now.

She opened it blindly, having closed her eyes as she did so. Her fingers felt along the edges until she found it to be a card and she blinked down at the image that looked back at her.

The illustration was of a colourful little bay, drawn by an artist to represent Positano.

It was almost worse than an image of Agatha.

She opened it to see loopy handwriting, much neater than her son’s.

Rio, Merry Christmas. You once told Nicky the color green was lucky. I hope this has some luck in it too. Agatha.

Rio frowned at the message, her forefinger tracing the loops of Agatha’s signature and feeling the soft indent of her pen there.

Any remnant of Agatha was now precious.

She put the card aside to pick up the gift that had been left beneath it and opened that in the same way she had Nicky’s.

Inside the neat wrappings was a box with the initials HW on the front.

Harry Winston.

Rio hesitated before she opened it, knowing that whatever was inside would be beautiful and expensive.

And it was.

Sitting on a deep navy cushion was a gold pendant necklace, with a perfectly round emerald encased by a gold setting. It was delicate and Rio touched it equally delicately, wondering when Agatha had decided she’d buy her a gift, wondering when she’d decided she’d buy her this gift.

“Rio! You bad child,” came her mom’s voice from the other end of the room, “You cannot open gifts now!”

Rio barely reacted and chewed on her lip as she closed the little box and picked up the cards and the wrappings.

“I need to shower and then I’ll be down for dinner, okay?”

Her mom just waved a hand in dismissal and Rio disappeared up the stairs with her treasures, depositing the discarded wrappings in the trash as she went.

When in her room she jumped on her bed and lay out her gifts before her like a collector admiring her latest finds.

She stared at each one in turn, wondering why it hadn’t crossed her mind to even send a card. To at least buy Nicky something.

But then, she supposed, never in a million years had she assumed Agatha would give her a gift.

She pulled her phone out and ignored the texts and calls that filled her home screen and found Agatha’s contact in WhatsApp.

7:14pm
Rio Vidal: I didn’t get the memo about exchanging gifts.

Simple. Casual. Letting Agatha know she knew she should have sent something.

She placed her phone down just as the response came through.

7:15pm
Agatha Harkness: A strange way to say thank you.

7:16pm
Rio Vidal: I should be saying sorry. I hear you spent the afternoon with my parents

7:16pm
Agatha Harkness: They were great.

Rio chewed on her lip, her thumbs doing their familiar dance over the keypad as she leant over her phone.

7:19pm
Rio Vidal: Can you tell Nicky I’m sorry I missed him?

7:22pm
Agatha Harkness: I will.

Agatha wasn’t giving much. But this was the first she’d heard from Agatha in weeks and she wasn’t willing to let it go so easily.

The lightweight metal of her battered iPhone felt suddenly heavy in her hands, suddenly precious because it was full of Agatha.

Casting aside her fear that Agatha might not even respond, she pressed on:

7:23pm
Rio Vidal: Why would I need luck?

7:24pm
Agatha Harkness: Your mom warned me you might open your gifts.

7:24pm
Rio Vidal: It’s beautiful

7:25pm
Agatha Harkness: The scarf or the necklace?

7:26pm
Rio Vidal: Both. Can I call you?

7:26pm
Agatha Harkness: My mother and in-laws are here.

7:27pm
Rio Vidal: I’ll see you at the CCAs?

7:27pm
Agatha Harkness: Yes.

7:28pm
Rio Vidal: Te veo

Rio put her phone down after that. Her gaze falling to the Harry Winston box and the image of Positano next to it.

She longed to be alone with Agatha again. Even if she couldn’t touch her. Just to see how she was. Just to know she was okay.

If she’d been nervous when she’d arrived earlier that day then that had to mean something. It had to mean she didn’t know how Rio would have received her.

It had to mean she cared.

Or she wouldn’t have brought her son. Wouldn’t have helped him write her card. Wouldn’t have gone to the trouble of picking theIr picture and getting it printed so Rio could keep it.

Wouldn’t have chosen Rio a necklace.

Rio spent the rest of the evening in a slight daze but tried her hardest to get more information out of her parents.

What she got was limited.

Yes: Agatha had spoken Spanish to them the whole time she was there.

Yes: her accent was good, yes she could teach Rio a thing or two about grammar.

Yes: Nicky had spoken a little in Spanish and where he couldn’t respond he’d used English.

Yes: he’d been shy all day.

Yes: every time the wind blew a certain way he’d turned to see if Rio had arrived home.

Yes: Agatha had taken Nicky away whilst Ralph entertained his parents and her mom.

No: she didn’t say much about it.

No: she hadn’t seemed bored or annoyed by her dad’s stories.

No: she didn’t try to leave quickly.

Yes: she’d asked how Rio had been.

It was flashes of an afternoon, delivered in rapid Spanish from her mother who was more interested in telling her about the family’s drama.

But it was all Rio had.

Agatha had told her she needed some time and Rio was giving her that. But she didn’t know how much time she had left in her.

But time moved still and before she could blink it was Christmas.

And Christmas Day was a soft day. A day where she could be in her pyjamas. A day where she’d felt emboldened by two mimosas with breakfast to send a photo to Agatha that went unanswered until the early evening.

She’d put her new necklace on even as she still wore her ratty old University of Delaware t-shirt and thrown the scarf artfully over herself too.

And she’s smiled like she might have done if the gifts had been handed to her personally by the people who’d bought them for her.

And in the soft lightning of her bedroom she’d sent the selfie; makeup free, and hopeful.

The response came much much later than she’d hoped it would.

9:13pm
Agatha Harkness: Green is your color.

Rio had been doom scrolling when the message came through, laid out on the sofa with a hoodie on over the pyjamas she’d been in all day. Her stomach was full and her wine glass was tragically empty but she could neither be bothered to refill it or bring herself to ask her mom watching Love Actually or rouse her sleeping dad in the armchair to get it for her.

Plenty of messages had been streaming through all day but this was the first she clicked into.

9:15pm
Rio Vidal: How has your day been?

9:17pm
Agatha Harkness: Fine. Yours?

9:17pm
Rio Vidal: Quiet

Rio chewed on her lip as she waited for a reply but minutes went by and nothing and so she pulled her hood up and sulked silently about it, wondering if she should have been more witty or asked another question.

At the top of her spiral another text came through:

9:33pm
Agatha Harkness: What’re you doing?

9:33pm
Rio Vidal: I’m on the couch. Mom’s watching Love Actually

9:35pm
Agatha Harkness: Maybe next year she’ll be watching your Christmas movie.

Rio frowned at this message, unsure what Agatha was referring to until her wine-slowed brain kicked into gear again.

9:38pm
Rio Vidal: Can’t believe you passed on it

9:40pm
Agatha Harkness: I have taste.

Rio smirked at her phone and danced her thumbs for a bit before she tapped back:

9:41pm
Rio Vidal: In necklaces, in women

The risk hadn’t paid off.

Agatha didn’t text back.

Rio sulked more and eventually took herself off to bed by ten thirty.

By the time Alice was back and the new year was celebrated with her parents leaving the day before, and with a messy, loud, house party to ring in the bells, Rio had blocked out her last, regrettable text to Agatha.

She’d been drunk out of her mind entering the new year and had just one more day of freedom before she had to get back to work with press events and fittings for the Critics Choice Awards on the 4th January.

And despite her reputation, Rio had remained true to her word.

She’d kept her hands and her lips to herself during her party.

She even kept her tongue in her mouth whenever Agatha was mentioned and as drunk as she was she gave nothing away and only nodded and smiled when people mentioned her name to her.

The picture of her and Nicky sat hidden in her bathroom cabinet and her precious new necklace sat on her vanity.

But her mind, her heart, they were full of Agatha all the time. Full of the prospect of seeing her in three days, full of the idea that she might be able to hold her hand, if only secretly, and for a few stolen moments.

And maybe it was the start of the new year. Maybe it was that she’d rung it in surrounded by friends. But she felt hopeful for the first time in a while.
